Preparatory Committee of the Pilots' Association Again Contends for Pilotage Sovereignty

The progress of our nation's recovery of pilotage rights is kept strictly confidential by the authorities, with all

news being unannounced, resembling the diplomatic approach of some nation's waterbirds. As a result, although the matter has appeared calm on the surface for months, secret negotiations have been quite tense. Since the recent publication in various newspapers of the Preparatory Committee of the Chinese Pilots' Association of this port, revealing the foreign opposition to the pilotage regulations and listing ten reasons for demanding revisions, exposing their conspiracy, and telegraphing the government to request a forceful defense, the inside story has been leaked, attracting public attention. Those concerned about national affairs are eager to learn more. Today, the reporter visited the association to conduct a conversation, and they recounted the situation, stating that our nation's pilotage rights between Tongsha and Shanghai have already been seized by foreigners, and the Chinese pilotage between Hankou and the Yangtze River is being suppressed by the Customs, not allowed to operate, and will soon follow the same disastrous path as Tongsha. This is because foreigners have a traditional plan to plot against us. In the 33rd year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, a foreigner named Tyler, in the name of the River Conservancy, presumptuously represented our country in granting the exclusive patent rights to the pilotage business from Tongsha to Shanghai to a foreign pilotage group, creating a situation where, in addition to our concessions, there is also the shadow of "renting water." Therefore, following the previous telegram, they again telegraphed the Executive Yuan and the Central Party Headquarters to request their intervention, and showed the original telegram, stating that the Shen Xin Daily reported that the Japanese envoy had been coming to Beijing daily to negotiate the pilotage issue, met with President Wang, and held discussions for as long as two hours, with very detailed exchanges. The inner workings are not difficult to guess. It is noted that pilotage is related to national defense and also to politics, so all countries attach great importance to it. The former Qing Dynasty's Zongli Yamen officials were simply sinecures, and naturally did not understand this, so it is no surprise that they continuously relinquished rights everywhere. Even the general public lacks research on this matter, so after navigation rights and pilotage rights were surrendered, there were even fewer who came forward to advocate for remedies. Tracing back to the seventh year of the Tongzhi reign, Robert Hart, the Inspector General of Customs, deceived the Zongli Yamen and approved the General Pilotage Regulations, so that all rights related to pilotage existed in name only but not in reality. Furthermore, since the 33rd year of the Guangxu reign (1907 AD), W.F. Tyler of the Shanghai River Conservancy

presumptuously represented our government and granted the exclusive patent rights for the Shanghai-Tongsha section to a foreign pilotage group in Shanghai, and allowed it to register in Hong Kong. Thus, China, in addition to the concessions, now also had "rented water." The above is only a brief account of the history of surrender. The most heartbreaking events were the Sino-French War in Minjiang, the Tianjin-Tanggu Incident, and the recent January 28th Incident, in which enemy warships were led into the port by pilots licensed by China. This is a rare and outrageous humiliation in the world. Past events are easily forgotten, but the January 28th Incident, then (titles omitted), from the Party's standpoint, was directly impacted. How could the association not be saddened by the inaction of the authorities and feel deeply about the folly of leaving the door wide open? As for the foreigners' excuse that pilotage is related to inland navigation rights, this is a completely unfounded fallacy. Not only has the association searched the treaties and found no basis for it, but many contemporary sages have also discussed and refuted its absurdity. With the sagacity of (titles omitted), who has a far-sighted perspective, why would the association need to cite numerous examples for him to finally realize? Even the only argument foreigners consider unassailable is the phrase "free employment of pilots" found in various treaties, which they use to oppose the recovery of pilotage rights. But it is well known that the treaty clearly states "free employment," which has been transformed into "free appointment." Isn't this the biggest joke in the world? Moreover, the General Pilotage Regulations approved by the former Qing Dynasty's Zongli Yamen were originally our country's internal affairs, and the government naturally has the right to change them at any time, as sovereignty dictates. Foreigners should not be able to interfere. However, since the government announced the Pilotage Management Regulations last September, the Inspector General of Customs

protested and demanded revisions. This is a clear demonstration of his contempt for the government and the traditional policy of imperialism. Subsequently, the consular corps opposed it, echoing each other, performing a farcical duet on the political stage. Finally, the envoys of various countries came out to bargain and reap the final victory. This is the political strategy of various countries in responding to our efforts to recover pilotage rights. Although the details of the Japanese envoy's discussions are not clear in the news, it is expected that they will not deviate from this pattern. How the government will navigate this situation is up to them. We will listen with respect. Since the Pilotage Management Regulations were announced and then protested and revised by the Inspector General of Customs, it has happened repeatedly, and each time, the opinions of foreigners are solicited first, which seems to have lost the autonomy of the system. Therefore, the content of the regulations is getting worse with each revision, so that the main points are essentially the same as the old regulations of the seventh year of the Tongzhi reign, merely a change of appearance without substance. For example, regarding the nationality of pilots, the old regulations of the former Qing Dynasty originally allowed both Chinese and foreigners to serve equally, but now, in response to foreigners, it is stipulated that the Chinese government is happy to employ them, with an explicit statement that foreigners can still be appointed. Although this sounds better on the surface, what is the difference in substance? Is this deceiving oneself or deceiving others? The association does not dare to say, but from the perspective of technicians, we believe that this approach is a fatal wound to our country's recovery of pilotage rights, and also a fatal wound to national defense and politics. Because if foreigners are allowed to continue serving as our country's pilots, then there will never be a recovery. Moreover, the government has not taken any action against the Japanese and Western pilotage groups in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River, and there are no restrictions on the entry and exit of ships over 5,000 tons. Although the dismantling of defenses did not begin today, the opening of the gates is more severe now than ever before. The association contemplates the future and trembles with fear. We also read President Wang's speech on peace and unity, which stated that the blood and sweat of the people should be used for national defense and external affairs. We believe that if the conditions for recovering pilotage rights are as bad as reported above, our country will be in a permanent state of being slaughtered. Even if the people shed blood and sweat, how will it flow? Furthermore, the late Premier created the Party and the nation, and his last words always regarded the overthrow of unequal treaties imposed by imperialists as the only policy for China's freedom and equality. Moreover, the National Government is a revolutionary government, and by definition, it should have revolutionary diplomacy. Is it pursuing revolutionary diplomacy on the issue of pilotage? The association's foolishness cannot fathom the depths. In the past year, we have repeatedly contributed our opinions to the government on the advantages and disadvantages of this matter, speaking with tears in our eyes, but there has been no response, as if the heavens are high and the earth is vast, and there is no way to appeal. Now, we venture to speak again, with the qualifications of citizens and the perspective of pilotage technology, and respectfully present two principles: (1) The nationality of pilots, no matter what, can only be Chinese; (2) All foreign pilots must be completely eliminated within five years, or at most ten years, and no longer employed. With this goal in mind, everyone from the head of state to the citizens should sacrifice their sincerity, dedication and enthusiasm. If this cannot be achieved, then any form of deception is like a country like this. Can it stand in today's competitive world? Should it be in (titles omitted). The association's alarmist words may be inappropriate for the times, and we know that we are guilty, but the situation is urgent and the enemies are deep, so it is difficult to remain silent. We are telegraphing in fear, awaiting instructions. Preparatory Committee of the Chinese Pilots' Association.

Ms. Luo Lun Specifically Explains the Marriage Advertisement

Those who need samples of [Hu Su Er] asthma medicine and detailed instructions for the radical cure of asthma, please write to the Shanghai Jiujiang Road No. 150 Foreign Building, Huashang Fu Ying Pharmacy, and they will be sent immediately.

The marriage advertisement published in this newspaper previously was intended to promote a unique and effective medicine for asthma, namely [Hu Su Er] asthma medicine. The use of "marriage advertisement" as a title was to attract the attention of readers. Now, in order to avoid any misunderstandings, a detailed explanation is provided below:

(1) Luo Lun is not a person's name, but the name of the Luo Lun Chemical Pharmaceutical Factory located in [Aisen City], Germany. The factory manufactures the asthma medicine [Hu Su Er], English name (FELSOL).

(2) There is no [Qi Ji Ping] University in Germany. [Qi Ji Ping] is a translation of [Qi Ji Bing] (asthma).

(3) Luo Lun Chemical Pharmaceutical Factory is one of the world's largest pharmaceutical factories, with a very large scale, rich assets, and a famous reputation throughout Germany.

(4) [Hu Su Er] asthma medicine has been in China for eight years. It is now exclusively managed by Huashang Fu Ying Pharmacy, and its sales cover the entire China. It is extremely effective in treating various heart and chronic bronchitis, cough, and asthma. Whether in the military, political, decision-making, or academic fields, all those who suffer from asthma consider it the only good companion.

(1) [Hu Su Er] asthma medicine is exclusively managed by Shanghai Huashang Fu Ying Pharmacy, and most of those who take it are Chinese, hence the mention of Chinese nationality.

(2) The age is specified as 18 to 30 years old because this period is the youth and prime of life, and various heart diseases are most likely to occur, or those in the academic field who do strenuous exercise may suffer from palpitations and shortness of breath, and should take [Hu Su Er] asthma medicine to be effective.

(3) [Hu Su Er] asthma medicine is the only effective medicine for treating various heart diseases, chronic bronchitis, cough, and asthma. It has the special effects of relieving chest tightness, pain, stopping cough, relieving asthma, lowering qi, and strengthening the heart, so it is praised by doctors all over the world. However, there are many fake medicines on the market with slippery properties. If one is not careful, it is easy to be deceived. It is hoped that everyone will not mistakenly purchase fake medicines and mislead themselves.

(4) There are many famous places in China. If one suffers from asthma and cannot walk vigorously when traveling, wouldn't it be a regret? Therefore, one should take [Hu Su Er] asthma medicine so that asthma does not occur and one can fully enjoy the scenery while traveling, doubling the fun.

Shen Bao Second Edition

Directorate General of Posts Scheduled to Move to Beijing

Detention of Private Letters Is Actually a Misunderstanding; Mail Service to Recovered Bandit Areas is Smooth

Central News Agency reports: The move of the Directorate General of Posts to Beijing was originally scheduled to begin on December 12th of last year, but was postponed to the winter vacation due to the issue of schooling for the children of employees. Yesterday, a Central News Agency reporter visited the Director of General Affairs of the Directorate General, Zhu Menghou, who said,

Directorate General Moves to Beijing

It has now been decided that the relocation will be completed within three days, starting on the 17th of this month. Currently, documents and other items have been prepared. A total of 140 employees of the department, plus their families, totaling about 300 to 400 people, will also go to Beijing during these three days. The Directorate General will resume normal operations in the capital on Monday, the 21st. As for the

Detention of Private Letters

In fact, this is a misunderstanding. The post office is only acting in accordance with the orders of the Ministry. All private letters sent before December 31st of the 23rd year will not be detained. However, after being sent by the sending post office to the destination post office, that post office will notify the private letter offices to send personnel to the post office to supervise the opening of the package and verify the number of letters. The post office will then deliver the letters to each household on their behalf, and after the delivery is completed, each letter will have a receipt stamped and returned to the private letter offices, free of charge, for verification. However, from January 1st of this year, if the post office discovers private letters again, they will all be detained, and if necessary, they will be punished according to the law for privately delivering letters and infringing on the national postal service.

Decline of Private Letter Offices

It began early with the development of the postal service. If private letter offices relied solely on delivering letters, they would not have been able to survive long ago, even before the Ministry's order to abolish private letter offices, they would have been running around appealing. The most developed areas for private letter offices in the past were Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, and their main source of income was transferring silver and foreign goods for customers. As for letters, the benefits were very small. The post office charges five cents for ordinary letters weighing no more than 20 grams, while private letter offices collect letters to a certain place, pack them into a bundle, and then hand them over to the post office to pay according to the weight. The benefit is only on the number of letters weighing less than 20 grams, which is very small. Currently, the Ministry's order to abolish private letters only applies to [letters]. Other original ancillary businesses, such as transferring silver and foreign goods, can continue to operate. Moreover, there are very few letters sent by private letter offices now, so the impact on private letter offices is not significant.

Postal Issues

Already resolved by commercial negotiation and will begin on the 10th. As each area of the bandit region is recovered, a post office will be established to forward letters. Therefore, the forwarding of mail from recovered bandit areas is now unhindered.

Restoration of the Siberian Postal Route

The Post Office has notified the Universal Postal Union

The Siberian Postal Route was suspended after the postal service in Northeast China was discontinued, causing delays. Mail from our country to Europe took more than a month for faster deliveries and almost two months for slower ones. It is now reported that the Post Office has notified the Universal Postal Union, stating that, in light of the resolutions of the League of Nations' Advisory Committee, and to reduce the delays in communication between China and Europe and the United States, the previously suspended postal route has been restored. All procedures will be handled as before.

Central Committee Member Huang Fusheng Cables the Central Government to Send Troops to Suppress Bandits

Hoping for the unanimous support of fellow Sichuanese. Central Committee Member Huang Fusheng, of the Shanghai Sichuanese Association and a Supervisory Committee member, was previously dispatched to Sichuan to inspect party affairs. Observing the rampant bandits in Sichuan and fearing the spread of the communist scourge, endangering the party and the nation, he specifically cabled the Central Government, requesting the swift dispatch of a large army to Sichuan to suppress the bandits. He also cabled fellow natives in Shanghai, urging their unanimous support to realize this goal. The original text is as follows: To the Shanghai Sichuanese Association, Gentlemen: I recently sent a cable to the Nationalist Government’s Executive Yuan Military Affairs Commission, stating: "Having been ordered to return to Sichuan to inspect party affairs, it is my duty to comply. However, seeing the communist flames filling the sky, the cries of distress echoing across the land, the hearts of the people in turmoil, and danger lurking everywhere, I am deeply concerned about the future. Therefore, not avoiding the appearance of overstepping my bounds, I present my humble opinion, to express my limited views, to the government. The communist bandits’ invasion of Sichuan was initially weak, with only a few thousand men and guns, causing disturbances only in the border areas. However, following the outbreak of the Sichuanese civil war, the bandit forces secretly grew. One misstep led to a great expansion. Now they are eyeing the Fu River, invading Youyang and Pengshui, and important towns and cities are falling one after another. The fire is spreading, and the opportunity for defense is becoming increasingly urgent. Both Sichuan provinces are in turmoil and unrest. Secret uprisings are frequently heard, and bandits are rising up in droves. Those with resources are packing up and moving their families out of the province, while those without resources are wandering aimlessly on the streets, crying out without any hope, a truly unbearable sight. These are all the people nurtured by our government, yet they unexpectedly find themselves trapped in this abyss of misery. Counting the times that the army has engaged with the bandits, for the past two years, the Sichuanese army, with 300,000 troops, has repeatedly encircled them, but the bandits, with only a few thousand remnants, have struggled against them, rotating in battles, but instead being taken advantage of. Recently suffering another defeat, the bandit forces have become even stronger. Supplies of rations and ammunition are difficult to replenish, and the soldiers are unable to get a full meal. The army is old and exhausted, and in a precarious situation. If they wish to succeed, they fear it will be hopeless. Furthermore, hearing that the bandits who broke out of Jiangxi, passed through the rugged and dangerous areas of southern Hunan, traversing two or three thousand miles, as if traveling through uninhabited territory, were able to safely occupy the border of Guizhou. This momentum is frightening, even stronger than when Xu bandits entered Sichuan. However, the current military strength of Guizhou province is weaker than that of the Sichuan army in the past. If they are not quickly eliminated before their wings are fully formed, and delayed repeatedly, they will again grow in strength, and accumulate into a second Sichuan that will be difficult to clean up. If they further unite with He Long and Xu Xiangqian's bandits into one force, then the Sichuan and Guizhou provinces will become a bandit den. Further, if they annex Yunnan, and occupy Sichuan, Yunnan, and Guizhou as their fundamental nest, then taking advantage of the overwhelming momentum, they will peer into the Yangtze River, and China's future will truly be lost forever. I have silently observed the overall situation, and considered it thoroughly. At this critical moment, and with the people's earnest hopes, I can only beseech our government, to think of the west, to swiftly transfer elite troops from Sichuan, Shaanxi, and Hubei provinces to Sichuan to suppress the bandits in separate directions, and also to swiftly transfer elite troops from Yunnan, Hunan, and Guangxi provinces, to jointly encircle the Guizhou army on all sides, to avoid joining forces with the Sichuan bandits, leading to an irredeemable situation. Furthermore, the government should appoint a knowledgeable military official to control the six provinces' supporting armies, enter Sichuan to supervise and lead the joint encirclement and suppression, and strive for practical results. As for the financial aspect, if the excessive and harsh taxes and levies, and the unrestricted issuance of paper money, two policies regarding currency, are not immediately stopped, and a method of relief is not found, then the good people in the non-bandit areas will be forced to take risks and seek a way out. They will also be forced to become bandits. Even if the supporting armies gather, the chaos in Sichuan will still have no hope of being cleared. I can only beseech the government to start from the political aspect, to quickly plan a fundamental relief strategy, to ensure that administration is staffed by competent people, so that corruption can be reduced, and the people's distress can be alleviated. Do everything to reverse what the leaders of Sichuan are currently doing, to rescue the people from the brink of disaster, and bring them to a place of peace. If we can do this, we will surely achieve the complete pacification and cleansing, without any worries or repercussions. The government previously said that the bandits in Jiangxi had not yet been pacified, so it had no time to look west. Now that the bandit lairs are about to be destroyed, the large army can move west, to relieve the people of Sichuan from complete inversion, and drive out the communist atmosphere from outside the borders. It is up to our government to make a decisive decision and save these common people. Now the people of Sichuan are drowning in misery, eagerly hoping for governance. They are preparing baskets of food and pots of drinks, both women and children are ready. It is easy to imagine that the hearts of the people are leaning towards the national army. Moreover, the Sichuan army has been defeated repeatedly, its morale has been crushed, its steps are not uniform, and its people have no goals. The national army acts as the rear guard, supervising and ordering the vanguard, not only achieving the effect of unified command, but also boosting the already weakened morale of the Sichuan army. The opportunity is ripe, with no need for hesitation. These are my urgent words, I beseech you to consider and quickly implement them. I am waiting anxiously for your orders." Please advocate for unanimous support, in order to realize this goal. Huang Fusheng bows reverently.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Instructs on Methods for Affixing Revenue Stamps to Account Books

At the latest, should begin on February 1st, and continue to affix revenue stamps at one dime each according to the regulations.

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, regarding the annual replacement and affixing of revenue stamps, issued a notice to all industry guilds in the city, saying, "Gentlemen: We recently received a letter from the Sauce Garden Industry Guild stating that the new Stamp Tax Law has been amended and promulgated, stipulating that each account book must be affixed with two dimes. If a new account book is used, should revenue stamps still be affixed according to the old regulations, or should they be affixed according to the new Stamp Tax Law? Please investigate and respond. "An investigation of Article 24 of the Stamp Tax Law states that the date of implementation of this law shall be determined by order. This new Stamp Tax Law is different from other laws that take effect immediately upon promulgation. Although the new Stamp Tax Law was promulgated by order of the Nationalist Government on December 8, 1934, according to the provisions of Article 24 of the law, the current Provisional Stamp Tax Regulations have not yet become invalid. All account books should still be affixed with a new revenue stamp of one dime each, according to the current regulations, which is not illegal. If, during the year 1935, the new Stamp Tax Law is separately ordered to take effect on a specific date, then the one-dime revenue stamp currently affixed to the new account book, whether or not it is necessary to affix two dimes at that time, according to Article 23 of the new Stamp Tax Law, the implementing rules of this law shall be determined by the Ministry of Finance, so we can wait for the implementing rules to be stipulated at that time, to determine the standard for whether or not to supplement the stamp. It is not a problem now. "Furthermore, according to a letter from the Travel Industry Guild, most merchants are accustomed to using the end of the lunar year as the end of the accounting period. Now that the end of the solar year has passed, and the end of the lunar year has not yet arrived, should revenue stamps be re-affixed to the old account books already affixed with stamps during this transitional period, or can they be affixed after the books are closed and replaced? Please advise." An investigation of the telegram from the Executive Yuan in May 1931 states: "According to the joint report of the Ministries of Interior, Finance, Communications, Railways, and Industry, regarding the resolution of the National Merchants' Accounting Date, the 23rd State Council Meeting decided that the end of January of the solar calendar shall be the general collection and settlement period. Such regulations are consistent with the usual time of year and are also aligned with the originally set collection periods at the end of May and the end of September, each being four months apart, and are considered to be evenly distributed." This association notified on June 6, 1931. The period for settling accounts at the end of the year has been determined by the Executive Yuan to be the end of January of the following solar year. Revenue stamps for account books should be replaced and affixed no later than February 1st of each year, to comply with the general collection and settlement period stipulated by the Executive Yuan. Many people in Shanghai affix revenue stamps to their account books according to the lunar calendar, resulting in being penalized for being overdue. All guilds must notify their members not to repeat the same mistakes. "The above two issues are related to more than one industry, so we are issuing separate notices to all, hoping that you will pay attention and pass them on to your members, etc."

The Public Donation for Emergency Relief Is Very Enthusiastic, with Wealthy People Donating Generously

Banks, Newspapers, and Stores Collect Substantial Sums on Behalf

For new members who join, the duty method will be based on the order in which they joined, and they will be added to the list of members who have already been drawn. (5) If a member on duty has an accident, he should notify the association in advance. (6) The association will print the commission contract, file folders, and other items, which all members should use. (7) If a person requesting assistance is designated to be handled by a certain lawyer, he should not be allowed to choose. (8) The necessary office expenses of the association (making commission contracts and file folders, etc.) should be borne by the Shanghai Lawyers Association. It was resolved to have Chairman Shen Junru attend the meeting of the Lawyers Association to request this. (9) If a person requesting assistance is willing to donate funds to the association in the future, he will be allowed to donate, and it will be used exclusively for handling assistance matters by the association. (10) The member on duty shall review the request for assistance in accordance with Article 4 of the detailed rules. If there is any doubt, he shall jointly review the case with the rotating member on duty and the chairman of the week. (11) The member on duty who receives the above request for assistance may hand it over to the member on duty on the next day to handle. If it falls on a Sunday or public holiday, it will be postponed by one day. (3) The office will start working immediately. Investigation of Leprosy Work in Various Places

Wu Zhijian Returns Home Yesterday

Mr. Wu Zhijian, the general director of the China Leprosy Relief Association, was invited by the National Leprosy Relief Institute of the United States last June to give a speech on the leprosy situation in China. He departed the country at the beginning of August last year. At the same time, the Nanjing Health Department took advantage of Wu's trip abroad and specially asked him to investigate the leprosy work in Japan, Hawaii, North and South America, and other places. Mr. Wu has completed his official duties after more than four months abroad and returned to China yesterday morning. The reporter met with him at his office yesterday and learned about the leprosy situation in various places in detail. He said that after he went abroad, he first went to Japan, staying for three weeks, and went to Takamatsu, Osaka, and other places to visit the Japanese National Leprosy Sanatorium. The buildings were very good, and the equipment was also good. It can accommodate two or three patients, and treat different types of leprosy, such as nerve leprosy and skin leprosy. In addition, the children of patients are separated, and a special educational institution like a school is established to accommodate their children, teaching them life skills so that they can be self-reliant in the future. Married couples who have been specially permitted can live together, but are not allowed to have children. There are seven larger facilities nationwide, with annual operating expenses of 2 to 3 million Japanese yen, all of which are paid by the national treasury. The United States is even better, with its largest national leprosy sanatorium requiring 600,000 to 700,000 gold dollars each year. The thoughtfulness of its facilities and the generosity of its treatment are even better than those of an average Chinese family. It provides whatever the patients need as much as possible. There is a volleyball and golf course in the sanatorium. Each patient's room has a radio, but the patients are still dissatisfied. He also visited North and South America, lecturing extensively. He returned home via Honolulu and other places. The facilities were all good, and the expenses were borne by the national or provincial and municipal authorities. On the other hand, our country has more leprosy patients than any other country, but there are no large-scale sanatoriums to prevent the spread of the disease. From my personal observations, if we want to eliminate this disease, we must have national power. As for the sanatorium planned by our association, it could have been built earlier, but the drawings were changed several times and have not yet been finalized. The funds raised, including those from Hu Wenhu, are estimated to be about 100,000. The site has been surveyed near the Dadongchang area, and the bidding for construction can be started no later than the middle of next month. It is expected to be completed in about half a year, and it is expected to accommodate more than 300 patients.

White Russians Celebrate Christmas Yesterday

The Da Mei Evening News reported that the 18,000 White Russians in Shanghai celebrated Christmas from today (the 7th) according to the old Russian calendar. According to the old Russian calendar, Christmas and New Year celebrations are thirteen days later than the dates commonly used elsewhere in the world. Since the Russian Revolution in 1917, the old calendar has been abolished, but White Russians who have fled abroad still adhere to it. Yesterday was the eve of the White Russian Christmas. The Shanghai Russian Regiment held a review ceremony at the shooting range at 10 a.m. The Director-General of the Municipal Council, Arnold, attended the ceremony and received the regiment's salute, and awarded the shooting prizes to the various teams and soldiers. Russian churches will hold prayer services today and yesterday. Furthermore, various White Russian organizations will hold celebrations in the coming days. Avenue Joffre is the center of the White Russian residential area. Yesterday, White Russian men and women were buying goods in various shops on the road. Russian shops will be closed today, and Russian newspapers will also stop publishing.

Shen Bao, Page Three

Major Theft Case at Chung Foo Bank

Electrician Secretly Made Extra Safe Keys with Premeditation

Stole Over 20,000 Yuan While Working During Leave

丨Hu Honglai and Two Others Apprehended in Zhenjiang丨

Opening the Safe

Hu Honglai, from Anhui, residing at No. 11, Kanglai Lane, Kangnau Road, had been employed as a coppersmith and electrician at the Chung Foo Bank at No. 103, Nanking Road. In July of the previous year, Jiang Shaosheng, the bank's manager, had Hu make a replacement key for the silver box storing the safe deposit keys, as the original was damaged. Unexpectedly, Hu, harboring malicious intentions, secretly made an extra key while making the replacement and hid it, waiting for a suitable opportunity for his illegal activities. Last year, when the bank was open for business, and there was a light fixture that needed fixing, Hu did not go to work at the bank. When the bank was open for business, and there was a light fixture that needed fixing, Hu immediately went to the bank to repair it, seeing an opportunity. He then recruited Ningbo natives Sun Ruifu and Wang Xiaohua to the bank. Using the key he had made, they stole the safe deposit keys from the manager's office and then stole 21,000 yuan in silver dollars from the vault before fleeing. They divided the loot and spent it. At the time, Hu thought that this matter was unknown to anyone, so he fled. Unexpectedly, last month, Hu's wife, Zhang Xiuhua, went to Ningbo for personal reasons, where detectives from the Public Security Bureau found a handgun in her luggage, leading to her detention by the local court. Upon hearing this news, Hu, fearing exposure, fled to Nanjing with Sun Ruifu on the eleventh of last month. In Nanjing, they met Shi Haiquan, from Dongtai, who notified Shanghai.

The Situation is Tense

They then fled to Wuxi, and later to Zhenjiang. While Hu and the others were fleeing, their accomplice, Wang Xiaohua, was arrested on Guangdong Road by Chief Inspector Lu Liankui and Chinese Detective Liu Shaokui of the General Investigation Department of the General Police Station. 425 yuan in stolen money was found, and he was handed over to the First Special District Court, sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment. Meanwhile, Inspector Lu learned that Hu and the other two were hiding in room 34 of the Dahua Hotel at No. 2, Erma Road in Zhenjiang. He then ordered Chinese Detectives Wu Hanzhang and Chen Yonggui to go to Zhenjiang with official documents, where they cooperated with the Public Security Bureau to arrest Hu Honglai, Sun Ruifu, and Shi Haiquan at 4:00 PM on the fifth of this month.

Brought Back to Shanghai

57 yuan was found on the three suspects, and 985 yuan in stolen silver dollars were recovered from the home of Sun Qian's uncle, Sun Gansheng, at No. 13, Tongzhou Road. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Criminal Division of the First Special District Court. Police attorney Wang Yaotang filed charges against them under Article 338 of the Criminal Code, stating that it was found that Hu Honglai had sent 4,700 yuan of the stolen money to his home in Shouzhou, northern Anhui. Sun Ruifu used the large sum of money

Marrying a Woman

(Currently residing at No. 15, Lane 488, Avenue Road,) As for the stolen money, it is still necessary to collect it from various places. Therefore, a request has been made to postpone this case, and to request the local court to bring Wang Xiuhua in order to investigate the stolen funds, etc. When questioned, Hu Honglai and Sun Ruifu confessed to jointly stealing and each receiving 8,000 yuan, while Wang Xiaohua received 2,500 yuan. The remaining 2,500 yuan was used jointly, etc. Shi Haiquan confessed to providing information without reservation. Judge Feng Shide verified the confession and ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody and the trial postponed for one week.

The Concession's Water Company Will Collect Deposit Fees Starting This Year

Friction Will Likely Increase in the Future

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, due to the impact of the global recession and rural bankruptcy, the living environment of Shanghai citizens is deteriorating. Various groups have organized movements to reduce rents. Landlords have not agreed to these requests, citing the lack of explicit provisions in rent reduction laws. While a few landlords have agreed to reductions, the central business district remains unchanged. Therefore, tenants have been passively accumulating rent arrears, and landlords are helpless. Although they can sue in court, it is too cumbersome. Traditionally, the cost of tap water installed in the houses has been collected and paid by the landlords. Due to the accumulated rent arrears, landlords have also delayed paying water bills. The British Shanghai Water Company, considering that the procedures for collecting water fees would become too burdensome and the losses too great, has decided to require a deposit for all tap water pipes, whether newly installed or already existing, starting in January of this year. The deposit amount will be based on the size of the house and the amount of water used. If water bills are not paid on time and the water usage exceeds the deposit amount, users will be notified to pay the fees. Otherwise, the water supply will be cut off according to regulations. This is similar to the Shanghai Electric Power Company's practice of installing electric meters. However, while this measure may prevent losses for the water company, future disputes over water cutoffs will increase.

Dissolution of Cooperation

Sanbei Company's New Ships Provoke Opposition from Other Companies in the Alliance

The Sanbei Company's new ship, the Mingxing, has been rebuilt and is scheduled to start running to Zhenhai tomorrow, also navigating to Ningbo, realizing the planned route. However, Taikoo, China Merchants, Ningshao, and other companies on the same route, which have been in an alliance for business cooperation to eliminate competition, now face a problem with the launch of the Mingxing regarding the existing cooperation. The details are as follows:

Alliance for Several Years

For the past five or six years, Taikoo, China Merchants, Sanbei, and Ningshao have formed an alliance on the Shanghai-Ningbo route, dividing the Ningbo route into 42.5 shares. Taikoo's Xinbei took 11 shares, Ningshao's Xin Ningshao took 11 shares, China Merchants Bureau's Xin Jiangtian took 10.5 shares, and Sanbei's Yongxing took 10 shares. Since then, the four companies have been sincere with each other, supplementing surpluses and deficits. In the past two years, Sanbei's Yongxing has been subsidized annually, while Taikoo, Ningshao, China Merchants, and other ships have all been subsidized. Since the formation of the alliance, all four companies on the Shanghai-Ningbo route have had profits.

New Ship Route

Although Sanbei's Mingxing's route is the Shanghai-Ningbo line, Zhenhai is the main port and Ningbo becomes a secondary port. Therefore, a special pier was built in Zhenhai. The Mingxing's business focuses on loading and transporting goods from Zhenhai. As Zhenhai serves as an inland port, goods transported from Shanghai to Zhenhai and from Zhenhai to Shanghai can be declared at the South Gate for export and can be exempted from customs duties. From now on, cotton and tea from Ningbo transported to Shanghai can also be loaded on ships in Zhenhai and exempted from taxes.

Difficult to Continue Cooperation

Taikoo, China Merchants, and Ningshao have expressed opposition to adding ships to the Shanghai-Ningbo route due to the launch of the Mingxing. According to the current business situation, the four companies can barely maintain the status quo if they continue to operate according to the original agreement. Now, with the addition of a new ship, one company cannot enjoy the benefits of two ships being subsidized. Therefore, Taikoo, China Merchants, and Ningshao have not convened discussions to renew the alliance agreement for this year. In fact, cooperation is difficult, and the alliance will be dissolved after the Mingxing starts operating.

Competition and Bargaining

In the coastal shipping routes, the Ningbo route has been the most successful in terms of unity and the most stable in terms of freight rates. In recent years, ships on the Dinghai, Tongyang, Chongsha, and Beiyang routes have competed and cooperated, benefiting significantly in business. However, after the launch of the Mingxing, according to various companies, the breakdown of the alliance will inevitably lead to fierce competition on the Shanghai-Ningbo route. Ningbo now has six ships: Xin Beijing, Xin Ningshao, Xin Jiangtian, Yongxing, Mingxing, and Hongxing. With more ships than cargo, a price war and competitive bidding are inevitable.

Oujiang River Gradually Silting Up Making Navigation Difficult for Ocean Vessels

China Merchants Bureau Plans to Move Wharf. Porters Petition for Dredging of Wenzhou Oujiang Port. Over the years, due to mountain torrents and mudslides, the Oujiang River has gradually silted up, severely impacting navigation. The China Merchants Bureau plans to relocate the wharf. The porters' association in the port city is alarmed, concerned that thousands of livelihoods are at stake. They have sent telegrams to various parties requesting dredging. This matter is of great importance. Recent information is detailed below:

Ocean Vessels Find it Difficult to Enter the Port

On the Wenzhou route, only the China Merchants Bureau dispatches the regular ocean vessel Hai'an. The Nan Shi Lian An Shipping Bureau's Yili also calls there on occasion. Other vessels are shallow-draft wooden hulled ships. In recent months, the Oujiang River in Wenzhou has experienced increased silting due to mountain torrents and mudslides, making the river shallower. At low tide, the draft is very small, only five or six feet. Therefore, ocean vessels from Shanghai to Wenzhou often have to wait for the tide and cannot enter the inner harbor to dock if they carry heavy cargo. Vessel entry and exit are very difficult.

Proposal to Relocate the Wharf

The Wenzhou branch of the China Merchants Bureau has found it increasingly inconvenient to load and unload cargo and passengers. Moreover, the original wharf is gradually silting up, making navigation difficult during low tide. Therefore, it has petitioned the head office to find a solution and relocate the wharf to a deeper area, allowing cargo to be loaded and unloaded without obstruction. The bureau has sent personnel to investigate and confirmed that the situation is as described. After discussion, they propose relocating the Wenzhou wharf to the vicinity of Zhuangyuan Bridge and building a new wharf, which would be a permanent solution. This project is currently under discussion.

Porters' Great Panic

After this event, the Wenzhou Porters and Dockworkers Union panicked. If the Oujiang River continues to silt up without dredging, it will indeed block navigation. If the wharves are relocated elsewhere, the thousands of porters and workers who depend on them for their livelihood will be deprived of their income. It would also lead to a repeat of the severe drought that occurred during the Daoguang era. Therefore, they have presented the pros and cons and requested the Ministry of Communications and the Shanghai China Merchants Bureau to oversee the dredging of the Oujiang River and prevent the relocation of the wharves.

Ministry Orders Swift Dredging

The Ministry of Communications has forwarded this petition to the Construction Department of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, requesting that they quickly dispatch technicians to the Oujiang River to measure and dredge the silted areas as soon as possible to prevent the blockage of the waterway. In addition, the ministry will consult with the Construction Committee to discuss the dredging work on the Oujiang River, aiming to complete it in the shortest possible time. The matter of relocating the wharves will be decided after further investigation.

Chen Xinfa Dies Suspiciously Body Turns Blue and Foams at the Mouth

His Wife Ding Confesses to Having an Affair Case is Confusing, Bizarre, and Extremely Complex

Chen Xinfa, a local resident of Yangjing Town, Pudong, married Ding in the eleventh month of the 22nd year of the Republic of China (lunar calendar). They had a good relationship for over a year. Chen originally did odd jobs at home. It wasn't until the thirteenth day of the tenth month of this year (lunar calendar) that he was recommended by a friend to work at the Pinghu Electric Light Plant. However, Ding was young and attractive, and was coveted by others, leading to an affair. Chen returned to Shanghai on the 23rd of last month (lunar calendar), and the couple was as good as new. On the 29th, they went to Puxi together. Chen sent his wife to her relatives' house to collect a field deed, and then Chen also went to visit a friend. They both returned home that night. The next morning, a sudden incident occurred. Chan asked his wife to boil water for him to drink, but she stayed in bed. By noon, his face had changed dramatically. Ding asked him what was wrong, but he was unable to speak. He died at 4 PM. The day before yesterday at noon, Ding, along with her husband's older sister's couple, Zhang Xingtao and Zhang Chen, reported to the Yangjing Police Station that Chen's cause of death was unknown and requested an investigation. Chief Zhan sent officers to investigate and found that the deceased's body was blue all over and foamed at the mouth, suggesting that he had been murdered. Ding was questioned to find clues. According to Ding, fifteen or sixteen days after her husband went to Pinghu, her husband's cousin, Chen Zhangying, came to her house and insisted on sleeping with her. Because she was alone at home, she did not object. After sleeping together for three days, Zhangying suddenly brought three unknown young men, all speaking the local dialect. One of the young men was about twenty-seven or eight years old, of medium height, with a square, white face, wearing a yellow coat, a yellow satin cotton robe, and a yellow felt hat. He raped me all night. Zhangying and the other two slept on the floor. They dispersed the next day. When my husband returned to Shanghai, I told him about this, but he did not say anything. Before he died, when he asked for water, Xu Fugen and Chen Chengquan saw it. I don't know what illness he suffered, and he suddenly died, etc. Chief Zhan considered that since there had been an affair, Chen's sudden death was highly suspicious. He detained Chen Zhangying for questioning. Zhangying denied bringing three young men to her house, but she knew Zhang Quanfa. The chief sent officers to arrest Quanfa, but he had already disappeared. Xu Fugen and Chen Chengquan were also summoned, and they also testified that they did not know how Chen died. The case became increasingly confusing and bizarre. The chief sent more officers to investigate and learned that a man named Zhang Rensheng had an affair with Chen Ding. He went to arrest him, but he had already fled. The chief ordered all the witnesses in the case to be sent to the General Bureau for interrogation. The body of the deceased was reported to the court by the local guarantor for examination.

Five More Shops Closed Yesterday Morning

All Engaged Lawyers to Announce Suspension of Business for Liquidation

Recently, Shanghai's economy has been in a state of panic, and all industries are depressed. Shops are closing down every day. Yesterday morning, a large number of shops announced the suspension of business for liquidation due to operating losses and an inability to maintain operations. The details are as follows:

Hanyuan North Goods Store

Hanyuan North Goods Store, located at No. 10 Jinkangli, Zhonghua Road, Chinese territory, is owned by Wang Hanzhang. It has been operating for many years, specializing in wholesale and consignment sales. Its business was quite good on weekdays, but recently, due to the impact of rural bankruptcy, business has declined and become sluggish, leading to an inability to maintain operations. Therefore, lawyer Zhou Bingyang was engaged to announce liquidation on behalf of the store. The announcement stated: "According to Wang Hanzhang, the owner of Hanyuan Yongji Store, our store is facing financial difficulties and cannot continue to operate. We have no choice but to entrust a representative to announce liquidation, etc. Therefore, we hereby issue a public notice to all creditors to register at our office within fourteen days for verification and calculation. All debtors are also requested to come to our office within seven days to pay off their debts in full. Otherwise, we will have no choice but to pursue legal action. This notice is hereby issued."

Lihua Hat Company

Lihua Felt Hat Company, located at Dongxinqiao, Avenue Edward VII, French Concession, was established by Rong Hanji. Initially, the business was quite good and sufficient to sustain operations. However, due to the impact of the social economy, business has been sluggish and losses have been heavy. Therefore, lawyer Chen Wenxiang was engaged to announce liquidation and call for offers on behalf of Lihua Felt Hat Company. The announcement stated: "According to the above-mentioned party, business has been exceptionally sluggish recently, resulting in unbearable losses. We have no choice but to close down and announce liquidation. We hereby issue a public notice to the company's creditors to register their claims at our office with evidence within two weeks so that we can settle all outstanding debts. Furthermore, the company and Rong Jun have previously guaranteed payments for others. We are now withdrawing from these guarantees. Anyone interested in taking over the store and assets is welcome to contact us directly. This notice is hereby issued."

Lao Tong He Food Store

Lao Tong He Tea, Food, Candy and Preserves Store, located at No. 292 Avenue Edward VII, was opened by Shen Xiangbo. Recently, its business has also been sluggish and losses have been heavy. Therefore, lawyer Jin Xiongbai was engaged to announce liquidation on behalf of the store. Yesterday morning, the following notice was posted at the store's entrance: "According to Mr. Shen Xiangbo, the owner, business has been sluggish and losses have been heavy recently, making it difficult to maintain operations. Therefore, we have specifically engaged your esteemed lawyer to announce liquidation and call for offers, etc. Therefore, we hereby issue a public notice requesting all creditors to bring their debt certificates to our office for registration within fourteen days in order to settle and calculate all outstanding debts. All debtors are also requested to pay off their debts within fourteen days and obtain receipts. Failure to register within the deadline will be deemed a waiver of claims. Failure to pay debts will result in legal action. Please do not make a mistake. Furthermore, anyone interested in taking over the store, assets, and goods is welcome to contact our liquidation office. This notice is hereby issued."

Fusheng Hat and Sock Factory

Fusheng Hat and Sock Factory, located at Pishaonai Road, Xiaobeimen, holds a significant position in the industry in the city. It is a large-scale operation, and the owner is Wang Jinsen. Its business was originally good. However, due to the impact of the market, it has become difficult to operate. Therefore, lawyer Zhang Fukang was engaged to announce the liquidation and sale of Fusheng Sock Factory on behalf of the factory. The announcement stated: "According to Wang Jinsen, the owner of Fusheng Sock Factory, he is currently affected by the market, his finances are tight, and it is difficult to maintain operations. He has entrusted your esteemed lawyer to announce liquidation and call for tenders, etc. Therefore, all creditors of the factory are requested to bring their evidence to our office for registration within two weeks, otherwise, it will be regarded as a voluntary waiver of rights. Furthermore, all sectors interested in taking over the factory are invited to visit our office for treatment. In addition to the announcement, we hereby declare as above."

Da Yuan Trading Company, Etc.

Ten-Yuan Note Suddenly Becomes a One-Yuan Note

A Schoolchild is Deceived, a Small Shopkeeper is Despicable

Xia Zhen, a doctor from Hubei, 26 years old, lives at No. 2 Changyuli, Lafayette Road, at the intersection of Latour Road in the French Concession. His son, Xia Anmei, 9 years old, attends Bide Primary School on Lafayette Road. On the morning of the 6th of this month, at 8 a.m., Xia Anmei took a ten-yuan note from the Central Bank from his father's pocket and took it to Tang Renzhi's (36 years old, from Jiaxing) candy, toy and general store, located at No. 1212 Lafayette Road, in front of the Bide Primary School gate, to buy candy and toy paper pistols, etc., priced at 12 cents. Tang, seeing that Anmei was young and could be bullied, took the ten-yuan note and exchanged it for a red one-yuan note, saying that he had no change to give. He said he was going to the cigarette paper store to exchange it. The child, unsuspecting, took the one-yuan note to the cigarette paper store to exchange it for small silver copper coins, and then paid them to Tang, who gave the child thirty copper coins in change. Xia, being young and ignorant, took the candy and toys he had bought and went home. Later, his father, Xia Zhen, discovered that a banknote was missing from his pocket and asked Anmei, who told him what had happened. Xia then confronted Tang, who denied it evasively. Xia then reported it to the French Public Conveyance. The Public Conveyance sent detective Yang Weisong to arrest Tang Renzhi, and recovered the original stolen banknote, verifying the facts. Yesterday, the Public Conveyance escorted Tang to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District, where Judge Wang Wangxu presided over the trial. Public Conveyance lawyer Fei Xizhen presented the case, charging him with fraud under Article 365 of the Criminal Law. The witness, the child Xia Anmei, testified in court, saying that he paid him a green ten-dollar note, and he gave me a red one-dollar note, etc. When questioned, Tang claimed that Xia had come to buy things, that he was doing business with another child, and that he did not notice the ten-dollar note. He denied the fraud. The court verified the testimony and ordered a postponement to the 11th for further questioning. The defendant was remanded in custody.

Two Ships Collide in the Huangpu River One Boatman Dead, One Injured

Chen Guichun Breaks Ribs and Dies Wang A'si and Others are Turned Over to the General Bureau for Legal Action

Chen A'chun, 51, from Linghu, worked as a broom vendor, hiring his fellow villagers Chen Guichun and Wu Guirong. Recently, they loaded a boatload of brooms from the Zhejiang mountains to Shanghai, mooring at the No. 67 pontoon at the South Pier in Nanshi. At around 9 p.m. the night before, the boat was unloading brooms to the Xun'an Wheel when it was suddenly struck by a charcoal boat loaded by Wang A'si from Dongtai, which was traveling south to north with the tide and intended to dock at the pier. The collision broke the bamboo tops on both sides and touched Chen and Wu. Chen Guichun suffered severe injuries to his upper body and lost consciousness in an instant. Wu Guirong was less seriously injured. The shipowner quickly sent the two injured men by vehicle to the Shanghai Hospital for treatment. According to the hospital doctors, Chen Guichun's ribs were broken, so he died yesterday morning. Wu Guirong is safe. The news was learned by Zhu Haisan, the captain of the Marine Patrol Team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, who, considering it to be a matter of life and death, sent police officer Fu Cheng to investigate. Wang A'si, the owner of the charcoal boat, and Wang's partners, Fan Xiaohu and the plaintiff Chen A'chun, were all taken to the team and escorted to the General Bureau for interrogation yesterday morning. The local Baojia was instructed to report to the court for a post-mortem examination.

Male Corpse Hanged on a Grave Hill

The night before last, in an open space on the Tan Family Cemetery Hill in Nanshi, a man of about forty years old, wearing a black cloth jacket, blue cloth pants, bald and barefoot, resembling a rickshaw puller, hanged himself from a tree next to the cemetery. The body was discovered by a passerby at 7 a.m., who reported it to the nearby police post, which in turn reported it to the Ximen Branch. The Baojia in charge was instructed to report to the local court for a post-mortem examination. The court sent a prosecutor to conduct the examination at around 3 p.m. yesterday and ordered the Baojia to prepare a coffin and shroud for the body from the charitable hall.

A rickshaw puller died after mistakenly taking an overdose of medicine.

He thought his leg pain was from running and overdosed on medicine, which proved fatal.

Yuan Zongren, a 24-year-old from Haimen, was working as a rickshaw puller at Dai Yulin's house at No. 4, Lane 121, Minhang Road. Yuan suddenly suffered from severe leg pain recently, and although he sought medical treatment, it was ineffective. He thought he had injured himself from running, so he bought a package of trauma medicine from a pharmacy a few days ago. He ate more than half of it, and the overdose caused poisoning. After his employer discovered this, he was sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective, and he soon died. The hospital reported it to the Hongkou Police Station, which ordered detectives to investigate. The body was then transported to the forensic examination center on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court dispatched Prosecutor Guo Wei, along with medical examiners Wei and Zhang, and clerk Wang Zuyi, to the center to examine the body. Chief Zhu Mengwei of the Chinese police first reported the previous events. Then, Dai Yulin claimed that he worked at Huacheng Tobacco Company and that the deceased was the rickshaw puller he hired. He only knew that the deceased had leg pain but was unaware of his purchase and consumption of trauma medicine. Xue Fuzhi, a tailor, claimed that he was temporarily residing at Dai's house and had seen the deceased swallow two spoonfuls of trauma medicine at the time. He advised him not to take so much, but he refused. After hearing the statements, Guo ordered an examination and determined that the deceased, Yuan Zongren, was a male and died of poisoning before death. The body was handed over to his cousin, Ni Wanshun, for burial. A small package of trauma medicine was handed over to the court's exhibit storage.

A gambling den was raided in Mayuan Lane

Twenty-one gamblers were arrested, and countless gambling tools were seized.

The harm of gambling is no less than that of floods and fierce beasts. While they were opening the gambling den at 4 PM, a group of gamblers who were placing bets followed them. The New Coins Minted by the Central Mint in December of the 23rd Year

丨9.05 Million Yuan丨

The Central Mint Auditing Committee reported on December of the 23rd year that the new coins amounted to 9.05 million yuan. The committee appointed chemist Ge Laide to conduct random inspections in accordance with the regulations. The fineness and weight were found to be in accordance with the silver standard coin minting regulations. Certificates were issued from (23)08184 to (23)09993, totaling 1,810 certificates. In addition, the Class B factory bars (880 fineness) minted by the Central Mint in December of the 23rd year, from 45217 to 48354, totaling 3,138 bars, were all supervised and stamped by chemist Ge Laide appointed by the committee in accordance with the regulations during their calibration. The fineness and weight of each bar were listed and recorded, and permission was granted for them to leave the factory separately.

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 7: Hearing Words, Hiding Tears, Selling Oneself, Complaining of Hardship, Carefully Seeking Help, Eagerly Seeking Refuge in the East

He sat among the guests with his legs crossed, looking at everyone's faces, and smiled, "The meaning of the word 'difficult' is very broad. It doesn't necessarily mean wanting someone's money, wanting someone's life, or restricting someone's physical freedom to be called 'difficult.' In fact, anything that makes someone feel mentally uncomfortable is also called 'difficult.' For example, Mr. Li just said that the good news has arrived for this lady. You didn't think that the so-called good news is actually bad news for this lady." Although he knew that Yueying probably wouldn't understand the word "bad news," he didn't want to say it too bluntly, so he lowered his voice slightly. Although Li Shilian didn't understand literature very well, he could understand the meaning of these two words, and he was a little surprised, staring at Cheng Zhiqian. Zhiqian smiled, "If I don't explain this sentence, Mr. You might be confused. Let me give you an example. Just now, this Auntie Hu brought this lady to Mr. Jia's house. They not only have hope for the future, but also have a small hope at the moment, which is that the waiter, Xiao Ji, had already promised them when he invited them last night that they would receive one dollar if they came as agreed. This one dollar may seem trivial to us, but it would be enough for their family of five or six to buy food for several days. When they have no other options, this one dollar can temporarily sustain their lives for a few days. So, Xiao Ji directed this lady to apply powder, rouge, and change clothes, and she did as she was told. As a result, they let others see her for free, and it is said that they were even kicked out." Li Shilian smiled and shook his head, "No, Mr. Jia had two foreign friends visiting him. He felt that it was inconvenient for this lady to be there, so he asked her to leave temporarily." (106)

Random Talks of a Traveler Returning from Hanyang

— Kangjianzhaifu

丨A New Life Reveals Vitality丨

"In heaven, there are nine-headed birds; on earth, there are old Hubei people." The notoriety of the Hubei people, and especially the prevalence of fleecing in Hankou port, has always made travelers shy away. However, since the New Life Movement has been carried out vigorously, the municipal administration and daily life have been completely renewed, displaying a vigorous atmosphere of national rebirth.

The streets are swept at any time, and even the alleys are free of garbage and filth. Public toilets are built underground, and at appropriate intervals, there is an iron railing indicating the "Door of Convenience."

There are no pedestrians on the road wearing hats askew, unbuttoned, or with cigarettes in their mouths. When walking, everyone walks on the left side, especially when going up and down the docks, they walk separately, in an orderly manner, without any chaotic crowding. Hired vehicles and horses are all priced at fixed rates, and under the supervision of the police, there is absolutely no act of fleecing.

Oddly dressed and permed coquettish women cannot swagger through the streets. In hotels, various moods and special odors that interfere with sleep and tempt people to fall are also cut off. General life is returning to rigor from romance, and is tending to tension from relaxation. The individual's licentious and unrestricted freedom is bound by "propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame." And the social customs and order have suddenly changed the long-standing old look! The above words are snippets I got from a conversation with a traveler returning from Hankou.

"Things are done by people!" Who says that the long-standing nation cannot take a revival starting point from this easy-to-know and easy-to-implement New Life Movement?

Snippets

— (Tianzai)

The more _________ people are, = the poorer they are in sympathy; the poorer people are, the richer they are in sympathy.

Snowflakes fall down, covering up the filthy world. It's a pity it can't last long.

A ruler can measure the length of things, a clock can calculate time. How can people's hearts be revealed?

Practicing Calligraphy

— Xu Haowu

When I was six or seven years old, as soon as I came back from elementary school, my grandmother would urge me to practice calligraphy.

The paper had already been found for me - a sheet that had been used to wrap things, spread out on the desk. Grandma held the [priceless copybook] with one hand and smoothed the paper with the other, then led me to sit down and copy the book.

Nothing else was a problem, except that my grandmother, who was watching over me, was sitting a little too close. So, whenever the corner of the room fell silent, and only a pale yellow ray of the setting sun moved quietly on the dust-covered wall, her faint breathing would pluck at the strings of my childish heart, often disturbing my temporarily sensitive nerves, causing the brush with its worn-out bristles, which I usually used to scribble freely, to become more and more flustered the more I tried to please, becoming so stiff and disobedient.

Grandma herself couldn't write the word "安" well, so the quality of the characters could be passable. However, she could never stand the unevenness of the lines, with straight lines turning into curves and diagonals.

Frowning, she told me to stop writing; drawing on her own experience, she slowly folded the paper into a grid of intersecting horizontal and vertical lines for me.

[You have to be extra careful! A scholar's child writing like this is like a cowherd scrawling in the fields, how embarrassing!]

Grandma - my kind and gentle grandmother - felt a pang of sadness in her heart when she saw that her child was uncared for and not making progress, and her voice trembled slightly.

What good people detest. Until her death, she always cared for me especially.

Sketch of a Fortune-Telling Stall

— Zhang Muliang

In a corner of the road, there was a small, rickety square table, and hanging on the front of the table was a piece of white cloth with the large characters: [King Wen's Divine Oracle, unerring, utmost sincerity and Tao...] On the table were scattered word scrolls, a white lacquered board, a worn-out brush, leftover ink, stationery, envelopes, a wooden box, and other items. Sitting in the middle was a fortune-teller with a figure-eight mustache, known as "Xiao Iron Mouth," wearing a pair of large, round, old-fashioned glasses, set against a withered and bloodless face, with wrinkles like streetcar tracks deeply etched on his forehead; but he was full of spirit, raising his worn-out brush, dipping it in the leftover ink, and painting on the white lacquer.

He spoke many江湖formulas, attracting people who often strolled along the road to stop beside him, gazing and listening like wooden puppets.

Xiao Iron Mouth's mysterious formula indeed worked. A young man emerged from the crowd, randomly took a word scroll from the wooden box, and threw it in front of Xiao Iron Mouth.

Xiao Iron Mouth immediately smiled, stopped speaking, and looked the young man up and down. Then, he raised his old glasses, wiped his eyes that could recognize heroes from humble origins, and said, [Brother! What do you want to ask?] The young man said shyly, [My wife is about to give birth, and I don't know if it will be a boy or a girl? So I came to your place to ask for a divination.]

Iron Mouth nodded with a knowing smile, unfolded the word scroll, which had the character [食] written on it.

[Ah!] Iron Mouth said dramatically, [According to the deduction of this character, your wife will have twins! Look! The top of the character 食is 人, and below is 玉, which becomes 金, so the first one will be a daughter. Look again! The bottom of the character 食 is 良, and if you add an ear to the right of 良, it becomes 郎, so the second one will be a son! Haha! Brother, you are very fortunate!] Iron Mouth suddenly stopped talking, his greedy eyes fixed on the young man's face, unmoving.

The young man only gave a bitter smile, seemingly wanting to say something but unable to, and took out about a dozen copper coins from his pocket, threw them on the table, and left.

Wavering in the Blown-Out Emptiness of Depression

— Yin Juan

The Piao Miao Record of Imperial Incense

— Original by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

How could it be that after decades of life in the palace, surrounded by countless tiresome etiquettes and ceremonies, even when she was asleep, she couldn't escape this encirclement, and yet she hadn't grown weary of it by now? One could say that she was playing tricks on herself, binding herself, not allowing herself any freedom of action: from morning to night, she was under the control of those formalities and rituals for not even a single minute. Even today's trip to the hunting grounds was still full of commemorative significance and couldn't be considered a purely recreational outing; the only difference was that today's ceremonies would no longer be performed in the palace but on another stage! Although this stage had a very close relationship with our ancestors, it was truly unfamiliar to us ourselves.

After a long journey, our large group of people arrived in front of the vast hunting grounds. After entering, according to the Empress Dowager's idea, we went directly to a palace. The construction of this palace was obviously very, very old, certainly decades or even centuries earlier than those palaces in Shengjing. Fortunately, people had been assigned to take care of it at ordinary times, so it hadn't collapsed; and before the Empress Dowager arrived in Fengtian, the local officials must have sent people to repair it again, otherwise, it would never have been so neat and clean! This palace was really just a rest room. Whenever a Manchu emperor came here to hunt, he would first enter this palace for a short rest, so that the people waiting on him outside could release the confined beasts, and then notify him to go out and chase them. When he was tired of playing, he would come back to rest again. But each time the delay was very short, and no leader had ever stayed here overnight, so the area of this palace was smaller than ordinary palaces, with only three rooms inside, and the construction was also very simple. (216)

Places Visited

On the Indian Ocean (Part 2)

— Zhang Ruogu

Port Said is divided into two major districts: in the European district, there are many skyscrapers with ivory-colored walls, set off by the verdant shade of palm trees, which is quite pleasing to the eye. The post office, banks, and large hotels are all located in this very international and modern district. Many mixed-race women of mixed blood leisurely stroll in the park or on the sidewalks, pushing baby carriages. For two whole weeks, we hadn't seen a single female figure on the ship, which was like a prison cell. Seeing those wives and daughters raised by the local whites was like finding an oasis in the desert.

The second district is the Arab district, where the streets are filthy, and one must hold one's nose while walking. At the intersections of the streets, there are many coffee shops, where locals wearing white robes and red round hats sit. Some also hold water pipes shaped like Chinese 胡琴, lazily whiling away the time. The streets are full of flocks of sheep like stray dogs, traveling in teams, accompanied by guards. In the vegetable market, one can see many Arab women, all dressed in black, never wearing brightly colored fabrics, their faces covered with black veils, unable to distinguish their beauty or ugliness. They have curly black hair, thick eyebrows, and large, round black eyes, glancing at us, their expressions extremely mysterious.

Most Arabs believe in Islam and must kneel in prayer five times a day. I did not enter the mosque because I had to take off my shoes and pay money. The area was originally under the influence of both Britain and France, but in recent years, Italian business has gradually expanded. Large stores selling Japanese goods are often seen in the city, and there are also many Japanese mail ships passing through.

I returned to the ship at four o'clock in the afternoon. I bought several local and Suez Canal scenery photos and developed the photos I took in London, which was not expensive. The fruits in Port Said are very cheap. Large, golden oranges can be bought for twenty for one shilling. With our old guide accompanying us, we got a lot of bargains everywhere. The old guide accompanied us for seven hours, and we each rewarded him with one shilling. He expressed great satisfaction and thanked us repeatedly before leaving.

The next day we arrived at Sabong, a naval port on the island of Sumatra in the Dutch East Indies, southwest of Singapore. According to the sailors, the place is a small village with only one lively street. The residents are Malays, and there are also many overseas Chinese from Fujian and Guangdong provinces. The main local products are fruits and spices. Occasionally, there are sales of sable, parrots, and young tigers. It is a pity that my luggage is tight, otherwise, buying strange birds and beasts and sending them to relatives and friends in Shanghai could also be used as New Year's gifts.

News: "Spring Color Bi-Monthly," published by Qianqiu Publishing House, No. 4, Lane 153, Carter Road, Shanghai, is rich in content and interesting. It features clear and beautiful nude art, valuable works by Zhang Yingchao, and excellent works by Zhao Jingshen, He Yubo, Hei Ying, Ms. Pingzi, Ms. Hu Yifan, Zhuang Qidong, etc. Each issue sells for only eight cents. The annual subscription is two yuan, plus a six-inch enlarged photo of nude art, sent by registered mail, free of charge. Direct subscriptions are accepted, and postage stamps are accepted.

Shen Bao Third Edition

Education News

The Central Government Plans to Allocate 1.5 Million Yuan

To Establish Scientific Museums in Gansu, Shaanxi, Yunnan, Guizhou, Ningxia, Qinghai, Chahar, and Suiyuan

▲Half of the funds will be used to expand teacher training and elementary education in each province.

▲Nanjing, July 7th dispatch: The proposal by Central Committee member Yu Youren to allocate 1.5 million yuan to establish national scientific museums in the Northwest and Southwest, to be first tried out by the Ministry of Education, has been reviewed by the Ministry of Education. The response states that the Northwest and Southwest are remote provinces and regions with vast territories, tight education budgets, cultural stagnation, and that vocational schools, normal schools, and secondary school content are mostly lacking in substance and incomplete in equipment, and should be subsidized to facilitate improvement. It is now proposed to use half of the funds to establish scientific museums in remote and poor provinces and to expand scientific equipment in secondary and higher schools. The remaining half will be used to expand teacher training and elementary education in each province. The provinces and regions to be subsidized will temporarily be limited to Gansu, Shaanxi, Yunnan, Guizhou, Ningxia, Qinghai, Chahar, and Suiyuan. As for the amount of subsidy for each province and the detailed regulations for its use, it is proposed to request the Central Committee to approve the principle of the above-mentioned funding, and then instruct the Ministry of Education to prepare and submit a detailed plan for review. After deliberation by the Political Council, it was decided that it was generally feasible and instructed the Ministry of Education to formulate detailed measures for review. The State Council has now issued an order to the Executive Yuan, ordering the Ministry of Education to comply.

Report on Inspection of Vocational Education in Beijing

▲Zhong Daozan Lists Five Points to the Ministry for Improvement

▲Central News Agency, Nanjing, July 7th dispatch: The Ministry of Education also dispatched Zhong Daozan to inspect the state of vocational education in Beijing. The results of the inspection have been reported to the Ministry. The report lists the main points that need to be improved, including: (1) Most private vocational schools have simple equipment and ineffective teaching methods, and should be strictly assessed. Those that are poorly managed should be ordered to close down. (2) The content of municipal senior industrial vocational schools should be enriched, and senior vocational schools should pay attention to practice. (3) The private Zhonghua Opera School should focus on the improvement of drama. (4) The annual income and expenditure of the five schools of the private Fanshan Charity Institution are barely balanced and should be reorganized. (5) The central government’s funds to the city have been distributed according to the new quota and should be quickly realized, as originally planned to expand vocational education.
