Situation of the First Joint Entrance Examination for Secondary Schools in Shanghai

▲The Chairman Personally Inspects

▲Good Order in Each Examination Hall

The joint entrance examination for the first semester of the 23rd academic year of secondary school students in this city began yesterday and was held in four examination halls: Shangwen, Wanzhu, Jingye, and Wuben. Chairman Pan personally visited each examination hall yesterday, and the order was good. Staff members of the office, such as Zhang Yongchun, were stationed at Lake Society and worked late into the night, which was quite tense.

Strict Supervision and Good Order

More than 900 candidates participated in the joint examination this time, which was held in four examination halls. Each examination hall had one chief examiner and four invigilators. Candidates from each school were accompanied by staff from the original school to the examination hall on time. Admission tickets were checked when entering the hall. Candidate seats were pre-arranged by the Education Bureau. Director Pan personally visited each examination hall yesterday and gave instructions on everything. The situation in the examination halls was quite good. Each examination paper was sealed and opened on the spot by the chief examiner, distributed according to the number. After the examination was completed, the papers were collected and sealed by the chief examiner, affixed with a private seal, and taken back to the Education Bureau and submitted to the Joint Examination Committee for separate evaluation and grading. Then, the committee opened the sealed paper and checked the name, which was quite strict. Today's examination subjects for high school are mathematics in the morning, geography and chemistry in the afternoon, and mathematics in the morning and physics and chemistry in the afternoon for junior high school.

Measures for Students Who Fail

Students who fail in all subjects in the joint entrance examination will not be allowed to graduate. Those who fail in three or more subjects should be required to repeat a grade, but repeating a grade is limited to two times. Those who cannot repeat a grade for some reason may be given a certificate of completion from the original school, stating the grades of each subject in the joint entrance examination, with a note indicating that they failed the joint entrance examination. Those who fail in two or one subject in high school may participate in the next joint examination in each subject, limited to two times. If they wish to continue their studies, they may apply for a certificate of admission to higher education from the competent educational administrative agency, stating the grades of each subject in the joint entrance examination, and they may be allowed to take the entrance examination for higher education first. After being admitted, they will be allowed to be probationary students. They will not be considered formal students until they have passed the next joint examination in each subject and have obtained a graduation certificate. Those who fail in two or one subject in junior high school may participate in the next joint examination in each subject, limited to three times, and may graduate after passing. If they wish to continue their studies, they may take the high school entrance examination with the same qualifications.

Method for Calculating Grades in Each Subject

The method for calculating the grades in each subject of the joint entrance examination is to calculate 40% of the graduation results of each subject in the school and 60% of the results of each subject in the joint examination. The above results are all calculated by percentage, and decimals are rounded up or down. From 80 to 100 points is Grade A, 70 to 79 points is Grade B, 60 to 69 points is Grade C, and less than 60 points is Grade D. Grades A, B, and C are passing grades, and Grade D is a failing grade. At the end of the joint examination, the Education Bureau will rank the average of the joint entrance examination grades of each student, the proportion of the number of graduating students in each school to the number of participants in the joint examination, and the proportion of the number of participants in the joint examination to the number of passing students into four grades: A, B, C, and D. Then, the average of the grades of the students who passed the joint examination in each school will be divided into four grades: A, B, C, and D.

Education Bureau Regulations on Rewards and Punishments

(1) Student Section: Students who participate in the graduation examination, achieve Grade A in all subjects of the examination and rank in the top three overall, or achieve Grade B or above in all subjects of the examination and are ranked in Grade A overall, the former will be awarded scholarships and certificates, the latter will be awarded certificates. (2) School Section: (A) Principles: Reviewing the performance of schools in the examination, the criteria are as follows: A. The ratio of the number of graduating students to the number of examination participants; B. The ratio of the number of examination participants to the number of passing students; C. The average score of passing students in the school examination. (B) Methods: I. Regarding rewards: 1. Schools that achieve Grade A in all three criteria (A, B, C) will be given a monetary reward; 2. Schools that achieve Grade A in any one of the two criteria (A, B) and Grade B in the other, while also achieving Grade A in criterion C, will be given a certificate; 3. Schools that achieve Grade B in both criteria (A, B), while also achieving Grade A in criterion C, will be given a commendation. (II) Regarding punishments: 1. Schools that achieve Grade D in any one of the three criteria (A, B, C) will be given a warning; 2. Schools that achieve Grade D in any two of the three criteria (A, B, C) will be given a reprimand; 3. Schools that achieve Grade D in all three criteria (A, B, C) will have the principal of the municipal school dismissed and the private school's registration revoked.

Graduation Examination for Middle Schools in Hubei Province

(Hankou Telegram) The graduation examination for public and private middle schools in the province and city began on the morning of the 7th, held separately in Wuchang and Hankou. Chairman Cheng Qibao, out of caution, decided to visit each examination venue in rotation.

Central Film Inspection Committee Jointly Searched for Supernatural Films with the Education and Public Security Bureaus Yesterday

The central government had long prohibited the production and screening of supernatural films. Since the establishment of the Central Film Inspection Committee, it has paid particular attention to and strictly enforced this ban. Shanghai is an area where domestic film production companies are concentrated, and it is also a breeding ground for the production of supernatural films. Although the central government's crackdown is strict, many small film companies still invest and take chances, secretly producing forbidden films of a supernatural, absurd, obscene, and theft-inducing nature, and privately transporting them to inland and remote areas of Nanyang for screening, only seeking to make huge profits, and disregarding the central government's laws and social education. Recently, the central government specially dispatched commissioners to Shanghai to handle the matter and investigate such forbidden supernatural films, in order to prevent private production and screening from poisoning society. According to investigations conducted by the Film Inspection Committee prior to the operation, they had identified companies that specialized in producing supernatural films. On the 6th and 7th, they jointly dispatched police officers from the Municipal Education Bureau and the Public Security Bureau to search each company at its registered address. It was reported that they seized seven film companies, including Great Era, Arhat, and Huadian, and confiscated many supernatural films. The confiscated forbidden films have been sealed up, and the companies have been temporarily closed, pending further action. It is reported that these forbidden films will be sent to Nanjing by the Film Inspection Committee for processing within the next few days.

This City's Primary and Secondary School Teachers and Students are Prohibited from Using Imported Goods

The Municipal Party Department Stipulates Six Measures

A Letter to the Municipal Education Bureau Instructing All Schools to Take Note

The Executive Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, stating: "Regarding the report from the Third District Party Department of this Committee, stating that the Thirteenth Branch Department has requested that teachers and students of all schools be strictly ordered to prohibit the use of imported goods, in order to prevent economic leakage and save the country from peril, etc., which was forwarded to this Committee. This Committee has drafted six implementation measures, which were approved by the 153rd Standing Committee meeting and forwarded to the Education Bureau, etc., as recorded. In addition to replying, a copy of the implementation measures is enclosed for reference and action."

Attached are the following implementation measures: (1) In daily life, domestic goods should be prioritized. (2) Notify domestic goods manufacturers to offer preferential prices to teachers and students. (3) Conduct regular (at least twice a year) inspections of the use of domestic goods by teachers and students in each school. (4) Publish the inspection results in the newspaper. (5) Those who use domestic goods entirely will be rewarded (the method will be formulated separately). (6) Those who willingly use foreign goods will be warned for the first offense, have 10% of their salary deducted for the second offense (the deducted money will be used for aviation donations or recorded as a demerit), and be dismissed or removed from their position by the school for the third offense.

Lectures on Career Guidance for Primary and Secondary School Graduates

To be Held Separately for Primary and Secondary Schools on the 13th of This Month

The Municipal Education Bureau Instructed All Schools to Attend the Lectures Yesterday

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau instructed the principals of all primary and secondary schools in the city: "This Bureau previously instructed all schools on December 27, 1934, in the morning newspaper announcement column, to return the number of graduates for this semester to the Third Section of this Bureau, so as to prepare separately for lectures on admission to primary and secondary schools and career guidance. Now that this semester is coming to an end, the lectures have been scheduled for January 13 (Sunday) at the Municipal Wuben Girls' Middle School on Huangjia Road and the Municipal He'an Elementary School on Xinzha Road North Chengdu Road. All graduating students from junior primary schools in each school will not participate. Those graduating from senior primary schools and junior and senior middle schools must attend the lectures at the designated venues and times, led by the principal or other important school officials. If there are any absences among the students who are required to attend the lectures, the school officials in charge must report the reasons for investigation. In addition to attaching a list of the lecture times, locations, and the names and numbers of graduates, all principals are hereby instructed to comply."

Special Article

A Review of the Rejuvenation Week at Shanghai North Middle School (Continued) Tang Naikang

(2) Methods A. Conduct individual talks and group lectures. Individual talks are conducted separately by the director of student affairs, student affairs officers, and other relevant teachers. Group education is carried out during memorial weeks, various commemorative meetings, or temporary gatherings. B. Guest Lectures. Invite well-known people from outside the school to give lectures on the essentials of self-cultivation or international issues to awaken students' attention to international political trends and improve their learning efficiency. C. Implement the New Life Movement. Since the promotion of the New Life Movement in this city, the school has taken this as one of the guiding principles of moral education and has made unremitting efforts to promote it. Successively held general meetings of all teachers, staff, and students to clarify the true meaning of the new life. D. Visit student families and issue questionnaires to connect with families. The purpose of education is to enable students to achieve balanced development in intelligence, personality, and physical fitness to cultivate healthy citizens. However, the student's personality is best known to the family members. Therefore, the school regards visiting families as a kind of moral education method and issues questionnaires to clarify the family environment of the students and provide appropriate guidance.

(C) Physical Education The school advocates universal training in physical education and strives to avoid distorted development. This year, a physical education director was specially appointed to take charge. The daily training is divided as follows:

(1) Morning Exercises Morning exercises are held twice. The first time is from 6:30 to 7:00 AM for boarding students. The second time is from 7:30 to 8:00 AM for day students. The general affairs, academic affairs, and student affairs offices assign staff to take attendance. Those who intentionally do not attend will be considered truant.

(2) Regular Classes Follow the standards set by the ministry, allocate teaching materials, and train students of all levels.

(3) Extracurricular Training Prescribe mandatory extracurricular items and minimum standards.

Divided into track and field events, ball games, etc., divided into teams and groups, practice once every morning and evening. Before the end of the semester, hold championship competitions to test the results.

(4) Physical Examination Conduct twice each semester, held separately at the beginning and end of the semester.

(5) Boy Scout Training All junior high school students receive Boy Scout training. Indoor teaching and field practice are equally important.

(D) Student Life People cannot live independently apart from the group. The importance of group life is advocated by scholars at home and abroad. The school believes that after the young students leave the school, they will all be members of society. Group life is essential for training. Therefore, within a reasonable scope, we provide guidance to enable it to develop. A brief description is as follows: (1) Grade Associations Each grade has a grade association, which is organized by the elected officials of each grade, in order to promote the progress of fellow classmates and the harmony of feelings. (2) Harmonica Society Music is a powerful tool for cultivating temperament, and the harmonica is easy to learn. Therefore, there is an organization of the Harmonica Society. (3) Xiaoshe. Xiaoshe is organized by students who love literature and social sciences. Members write articles on their reading experiences every week and publish them once as a forum for expressing their thoughts. (4) Hiking Team. Students of all grades freely organize and often travel together on Sundays and holidays. Their footprints have spread to Wusong, Gaoqiao, and other places with elegant scenery. (5) Sports Organizations Sports organizations have shown a vigorous atmosphere in the school. At present, there are fitness teams, black cat teams, track and field teams, football teams, volleyball teams, basketball teams, etc. Inter-grade competitions are held once each semester.

(4) Conclusion

The above are all general conditions of the past year. Looking at the past is to plan for the future. The Republic of China in 1935 will soon appear before our eyes. The various facilities of the school will also develop accordingly. The first step of rejuvenation has come to an end. What we are managing from now on is the second step of development, such as improving moral education, enriching equipment, and expanding student enrollment. We will do our best to realize it in order to live up to the good intentions of people from all walks of life. Those who are wise in the world are fortunate to correct them. (End)

Page 13

Free Talk

The Social Nature and Freedom of Art

— Canyue

Advocates of artistic freedom often conflate the freedom of art in its creative construction with the freedom of art within social conditions, attempting to eliminate the social nature of art. However, artworks are products of society, not things that fall from the sky. This is undeniable. The so-called limits of artistic freedom can only exist within the scope of its own development within various social conditions. Whether a writer creates consciously or unconsciously, artworks cannot exist apart from the formation or limitations of these many social conditions. Artists can only exercise their creative freedom within this scope. Even if a creator has a vast and boundless realm in their mind's eye, they still cannot transcend this reality. All ideals and fantasies are determined by real conditions.

If it is said that art has a special independence, then this independence refers to the expressive techniques of the writer in the process of creation (the process of artistic construction). This is the independence of the external artistic conditions that the artist bestows upon the artwork, not the trans-social independence of the artwork. The freedom in the artistic creation process is not only valued by those who cling to art, but also valued by all writers. Naturally, when creating, one does not need to consider various restrictions and can act arbitrarily. An artist only needs to expand his creative world during creation and can ignore many constraints (naturally, one must first have accurate observation). For example, when a person writes an essay, he does not need to consider various grammatical conventions, but every article can always be analyzed using grammatical conventions, unless it is a kind of delirium.

This freedom of [think as much as you can imagine, write as much as you can write] is the freedom of the creator during their artistic creation. However, those who advocate the theory of pure artistic freedom believe that because an artist has the free will to create a work, the evaluation of this work should be based on the level of the artist's cultivation and the degree of [artistic quality] given to the work. This view is neglecting the fundamental. It is not known that although the artist's emotions and the application of techniques in the work have unlimited freedom, the artist and his work cannot but be deposited in society. The first condition that should be limited is determined by society. In the structural content and the imagination of the story of [Robinson Crusoe], the writer had extremely free expression, which was successful in terms of art. However, what determined this artistic success and enabled the author to construct such an adventurous and absurd content was the social thought of commercial capital expanding outward at that time, needing to find colonies. Having these social conditions enabled the production of [Robinson Crusoe] and enabled the author to use his artistic freedom to expand and arrange his imaginary story. The Monkey King thought he was very free to take a piss inside the Five Finger Mountain, but he didn't escape the palm of the Buddha. Because he [didn't know] and [couldn't see] the entire palm of the Buddha, he thought he had complete freedom inside the Five Finger Mountain.

During creation, the creator needs to understand this principle in order to gain a broader realm of freedom. He must apply his vision and thought to things that he has grasped with correct understanding and knowledge, so that he can fully use his freedom in the process of constructing the work. Of course, not being free is not good, but freedom that is blind will lead to waste and indulgence. An artist who cannot understand social trends cannot see broad social themes. As a result, he is only selling small and ingenious [genius] in a cage (intellectual and technical). On the contrary, a writer who has a clear understanding of the times and society will see a farther and greater vision. His range of things is wide and real. Therefore, the freedom of art is: the author can have the freedom of use in the process of creation, but the conditions that form the artwork are unfreely restricted by society. Therefore, the evaluation of artworks must be based on a social perspective. Apart from its social value, the [skills] of an artwork will have nothing to rely on.

The Last Sadness (Part 1)

— Mo Qing

Ah, terrible sadness, tonight you have drilled into my heart again! Although I have tried every means to avoid you, is enduring you the only way? Ah, why can't I become harder? Am I destined to be your prisoner for life?

Alas, distant person, I say, it is really useless for you to continue to follow me in my dreams. Although I once sent you into the deep, cold door with my own hands. However, wasn't that your own willingness, and wasn't it very comfortable? Why can't you forgive me!

Alas, poor person! I say, we can really part ways. Now, we are so far apart. You, you should go on your flat, wide road. As for me, let me walk my self-made dangerous single-plank bridge. Now, my life has deteriorated to the point of no return, why do you keep disturbing me so often?

Ah, now I live in this coffin filled with dead people. Is there anything to share? Since you have betrayed your own oath of failure, of course there is nothing to regret, and even if my life is worse than it is now, I have no resentment towards you. I only ask that you can forget it peacefully, and I will be cheerful and bright.

Here, during the day there are two meals of coarse food that I can't swallow, and at night, several of us roll together like dogs in this coffin-shaped, narrow dwelling place with a hole in the ceiling that is almost in an eight-shape. The roof is connected, and the surroundings are fixed with short wooden boards. Is it airtight? Cold wind drills in from the cracks in the tiles, passing back and forth over the body. Is it breathable? Yet I can't find a ray of light. Every day, I look at the dark coffin that brings in the [clang] [oh li gua] sounds, and the sobbing sounds of funerals never stop. And the earth-shaking vibrations of the giant wheels of the nearby large electrical factory shake this tired body all day long. It's like people are living in a turbulent, miserable fog all day long.

Ah, listen now to the long moans of the cold wind in the deep night, which has replaced the anger of the giant wheels of the electrical factory, surrounding and roaring. Harsh winter has already arrived, and I am still covered with a thin autumn quilt. Although I cover all the remaining single clothes tightly on top, I still can't stop my body from trembling all night long. Often in the middle of the night, I slowly take off my warm clothes from inside the quilt and twist them on my cold, stiff legs to keep warm. After a while, the upper body trembles again, unable to withstand the cold. Sometimes, I can't sleep all night, and I'm doing this work of fighting the cold.

Ah, under the tragic circumstances of this kind of life, I not only cannot rise up and roar angrily like the cold wind, but in this middle of the night, I put on my clothes, sit up, and sing this kind of sad tune. Am I not afraid of being ashamed? However, I can't help it. I tell you: I have already endured everything that can be endured, and I won't make such ugly groans. Ah, terrible sadness, I beg you to leave me from now on!

On this night a week ago, I also dreamed of your tearful scene that made me unable to stop crying. For years, my heart, which has been forged into steel from thousands of sorrows, couldn't help but shed tears all night long when I woke up. Ah, tell you: how much ridicule I have received from my friends for such tears! Now, who can I tell this time? Go away, you flickering! Don't give me any more shame with your ugly tears!

Ah! I tell you: You really don't need to disturb me anymore. Look: the night is long, and the dreams are endless! If this continues, when will I be able to complete my difficult journey? Ah, please forgive me, really don't disturb me anymore! Listen: the skinny dog lying next to me is also letting out a long, mournful howl in its dream. Let me go to sleep too! I used to say: Only in dreams will there be my peaceful rest. However, now I know that there is no rest or peace even in dreams. But I still can't help but let myself go to sleep. Just as when sorrow comes, although wine cannot dispel sorrow, one cannot help but drink.

Ah, cold wind that roars with anger, please be quiet for a while! Let me be quiet for a moment, even just a moment. Now, while the giant wheels of the nearby factory have stopped vibrating, let me take advantage of this rare opportunity to sleep well, so as to recover some fatigue. Waiting for the sky to dawn, I will grab myself up and work like a cow for others. I tell you: I am unwilling to see that short, ugly monster shooting out its sneering eyes that urge me.

On Nathan Road

— Li Ai

The plane leaves rustling the tune of autumn.

Hong Kong is dyed with the deep colors of autumn.

Emerging from the hospital, everything felt foreign. Like waking from a dream – a heart-wrenching sorrow!

Carrying a weary heart, I walked alone on Nathan Road.

The locust trees were old, standing anciently on the asphalt road; the autumn sunset, like melancholy pearls, gazed upon the steeple of the church, the chimneys of the factories, the aged locust trees; purple old waves rippled on the asphalt road; British sailors walked jauntily, arms swinging, whistling, whistling the tune of "Ramona," Spanish senoritas waited in front of the cinema – a quarter past seven. The eyes of the rickshaw pullers, like hungry wolves, prowled in the dark streets.

Pale yellow streetlights struggled in the twilight, red electric advertisements cast bloody shadows under the aged locust trees…

The Nathan Road at night is mad; my own heart is lonely.

Having fallen from the cutting edge of life, I climb up, struggle again, once, twice, three times... weary; unable to climb up, the hammer of life falls on my head, I rise in disarray, struggle... endlessly like this.

Tomorrow's present, on the wheel, will pass through a green ocean to a strange place. Over the years, hope has vanished with time, and a gray shadow has been painted into the chapters of my life. So often I have tried so hard to grasp! What I have grasped is but a wisp of smoke!

Oh, you who are weary of life!

[...The South, rippling with a lively atmosphere, the detestable colors have already tainted our pupils. Come quickly, cross the sea, here there is fresh air... Man, you should be certain: behind the harsh winter, there is the smile of spring, this is the era of [strength], this is the year of struggle...] Thinking of Luo's letter, like drinking a glass of brandy, I secretly thank him, this friend who encourages me.

In any case, I will leave tomorrow, although I am recovering from an illness; but for the sake of life, for the sake of new hope that is enticing me. Hong Kong, in my life's history, is a page of bloody impressions, indelible impressions, but tomorrow's present will become the past, the eternal past.

I raised my head: the sunset was buried by the night. The lamplight cast my shadow on Nathan Road, blurred; I looked at my blurred shadow...

A black shadow flashed past—

[Man, oh! It's you!] Two hands grabbed me.

I was startled.

Beneath the disheveled hair, two dark, large, sunken eyes flashed, a straight nose, a wide mouth, a coarse beard, set against a lean, rectangular face.

I stared in surprise for a while, unable to speak.

[Have you forgotten? It's me – Lao Tie.]

[Oh], like a hammer falling on my head, I almost fainted! I would never have thought Lao Tie would become like this!

We talked about the past, the present, the future... We lowered our heads, silently looking at our blurred shadows...

Five years ago, we were both young men, we had the same ideals, the same expectations for tomorrow.

I thought silently about the different encounters each of us had...

[Yu Man, I can't talk much longer]. He looked at his watch: [It's eight o'clock, I have to rush to catch the night boat home]. He ran frantically, I caught up and grabbed him:

[You still want to go home?] Home?

[Oh, where else can I go?] Fire flashed in his sunken eyes: [No relatives, no friends—! I want to find my mother, oh! I destroyed my mother's lifelong happiness. In the end, I am willing to destroy myself for her... Man, forgive me, I am ashamed, I understand everything, but I cannot understand myself...]. Each word seemed to pierce my heart like a sharp blade; when did he run off? I didn't know, I hastily raised my head and looked:

He was running frantically, his shadow blurring, mingling with the dark street; finally, he raised a hand in the darkness of the darkness:

[Man! Farewell, life is like smoke].

Paradise Lost

— Lu Fen

Chinese people, especially modern Chinese people, often take "The present is not like the past" as a topic for their writings. Although it has become a cliché, there will still be many articles written about it. I am also Chinese, and I am more or less inevitably infected with this habit. How did I get this habit? Since when? I am really confused about it myself; I can't really explain it. If you must ask, I can only say that it started from losing paradise. The more I talk, the more bizarre it sounds. How could I possibly have a paradise? This is just intentionally exaggerating. The paradise we speak of is just the place where we played when we were young. This place may be very different from the paradise of heaven, because I have not yet been to the paradise of heaven, and I can't imagine what it is like, so I regard the place where I played as a child as paradise.

However, that paradise was lost without me knowing it, and because I don't have a paradise like heaven, I always think about that place with longing.

Villagers rarely have opportunities to entertain themselves throughout their lives, at least in my ancestral home that was the case. At the Dragon Boat Festival, they don't drink realgar wine. In mid-autumn, they don't admire the moon. On the fifteenth day of the seventh lunar month, during the "Ghost Festival," cities release river lanterns, but this is the countryside, without any organizations like "associations" or "societies," and there is no river, except for the customary burning of paper money when visiting graves, it is no different from ordinary days. Only on the Lantern Festival, children are overjoyed to get a paper lantern, and occasionally someone is willing to spend money to buy two small "firecrackers" to set off, which almost mobilizes the entire village. Playing dragon lanterns and setting off fireworks are things that even the elderly have never mentioned having done. This village is so small and so poor that it has never had anything big worth recording. The whole year is surrounded by a quiet atmosphere, and the situation can only be described as desolate and lonely.

However, the children are no different from those in other villages, and they never allow loneliness to weigh heavily on them, letting time pass in vain. The children will never sit by the adults, listening to them talk about the prices of rice, oil, and salt, anecdotes about certain scholars, or tales of ghosts and monsters, all of which are meaningless nonsense, unrelated to the hearts of the children. The children have their own world, which is on the threshing floor. Every year after autumn, the threshing floor is cleaned up and tidy, the moon shines on the bare and flat surface, and after dinner it becomes lively. This is the children's paradise.

Although it is just a threshing floor without any real or illusory changes, once it is occupied by the children, it will never be simple again. They can come up with many tricks, one of which is called "Old Turtle Sunning its Shell," which requires four people to stand upright at the four corners, with one person going up, stepping on the shoulders of the two people behind them, grabbing the shoulders of the two people in front of them, and running forward in one breath, somewhat similar to forming a human pyramid. There is also one called "Mouse Drilling Through the Circle," and many others that involve setting up defensive positions, answering questions back and forth, and then determining the winner based on the strength of their powers. Most places have the same games, only the names may be different. Since I am not doing research, I will not list them one by one. These games are mostly very childish, and the changes are very simple, but the village children play with all their hearts, and the sound of laughter and noise often startles the sleeping crows in the cold forest.

The Fly (7)

— By Pirandello, Translated by Xi Dichén

[We were to be married on the same day...! ]

[Don't be afraid, we will be married together!] Nelly said, while holding the man's head tightly.

At the same time, the doctor kept looking at the dying man, very clear, it was anthrax.

[Tell me, do you remember being bitten by an insect?]

[Didn't bite,] Chai Lu shook his head to indicate.

[Insect?] Salo asked.

The doctor explained the disease to the two farmers as best he could. It must be that some livestock died of anthrax. Who knows how many insects, perhaps swarming on that abandoned, stinking corpse in the ditch, and certainly one of them later flew around and transmitted the disease to Chai Lu who was lying in the stable.

As the doctor was saying this, Chai Lu turned his face to the wall.

No one knows it, but death is there; it is so small, so even if someone thought of looking for it, they simply could not detect it.

It is a fly, on that wall, seemingly motionless, but on closer inspection, one can see it sometimes expelling and sucking in its tiny sucking organ, and sometimes nimbly washing its two slender forelegs, rubbing them together, as if satisfied.

Chai Lu noticed it, staring tightly at it.

A fly –

Maybe it's this one, maybe it's another one. Who knows? Now that he hears the doctor mention it, he seems to remember. Indeed, when he was lying down here yesterday, waiting for his cousins to peel the almonds from Lopa, a fly had bothered him. Could it have been this one?

He saw it suddenly fly up, and he followed it with his eyes.

Flour Sales Lively, Standards Rising

After the flour market opened yesterday morning, the market for all months showed a consistent and stable trend. Quotations for foreign wheat were around two to three jiao higher for Chicago wheat, and eight fen to one jiao higher for Canadian wheat. When the prices opened, the quotations for foreign wheat were good, and current sales were quite active. It is said that the Tianjin group found the routes around Ping Sui to be quite busy, so the standards were adjusted, and the market was very lively. Therefore, the opening price situation was already stable. As for the forward months, because there were not many factories making up for short positions, the asking prices were very stable, about one fen to one and a half fen higher than the closing prices of the previous day. When the afternoon session opened, the market was calm due to active spot sales in the current month. The forward months were also initially strong, but then the buying interest turned quiet, and the prices fell back. According to observations by people in the industry, it is feared that the recent good actual sales will make it difficult for prices to fall too much. As a result, the current month rose by 7.5 li, February was up by one fen, March was up by 2.25 fen, April was up by 1.5 fen, May was up by one fen, and June was up by 0.5 fen.

Wheat Futures Rise Then Fall

Yesterday's wheat futures market showed a trend of rising first and then falling in both the morning and afternoon sessions. Quotations for foreign wheat were around two to three jiao higher for Chicago wheat, and eight fen to one jiao higher for Canadian wheat. When the prices opened, the market was very active with buyers and few sellers, so the asking prices were secretly raised by three or four fen. March contracts jumped by as much as eight fen due to buyers competing to buy. However, the trading volume in each session was not very large. When the afternoon session opened, it was initially firm, but then the flour market softened slightly, and sellers suddenly poured out, and the trading volume in each session was also unusually active. As a final result, the current month fell by four fen, February fell by three fen, March rose slightly by one fen, and the rest were not opened. In the current wheat market, factories are mutually exclusive, and there is still no delivery seen.

Chicago wheat: The visible supply announced on Monday is expected to have a large decrease. The need for spot and futures seemed to be improving when the price fell.

River Rice Stable, No Special Changes

(Hu Nan) A total of more than 30 groups arrived from various origins (with a total of nearly 6,000 shi of goods). Sales are still sluggish, and the situation is bland. The price of late rice has not changed much, only the thick japonica rice has been slightly raised due to the inferior source. People's sentiments no longer seem as firm as before. It is difficult to make a definitive statement about the current market situation and rely solely on the weather for a turnaround. Du Yang Jian is still lacking in goods and without a market, and Yin Bian Yuan is also just average.

(Hu Bei) Yesterday, only about 10 shipments arrived from various ports downriver. In terms of market sales, green brokers sold to fellow traders first, which caused customers to enter the market very late. Sales were weak, and the market was dull. The market shape of white glutinous rice was firm in the early market but turned flat in the afternoon market. Yang Jian was raised and killed off the market quickly. It continued to rise by two or three jiao. The remaining goods were all stable.

Foreign Indica Rice Sales in the Mainland are Active Again

期洋米續有大批成交 期 Foreign Indica Rice Continues to See Large Transactions

Yesterday, the foreign rice market was originally stable, but due to the continuous arrivals these days, the previously determined prices will gradually offset the costs, and foreign merchants are very eager to sell. The current foreign rice is now at a small discount of five fen. As there is demand for forward rice in both this street and the mainland, although foreign merchants are selling as much as possible, they are unwilling to sell at low prices due to high costs. Therefore, market prices can still be maintained. Yesterday, 4,000 bags of spot goods were opened, and 4,800 tons of futures were sold by Yali Foreign Firm and 500 bags were sold by Dafu, with more volume in the distant April and May contracts.

客秈以上游水淺、成本加高、到頭不湧、而昨日内地胃口甚香、且本街亦有應酬、天津問津客元、崇沙辦砶米、無錫辦新糙米、故市　甚俏、行情步砌二三分、全市開出湖南沙市各米六千五百包、 Due to shallow upstream waters and higher costs, the arrival of goods of guest indica rice is not surging. 又訊、洋米午後略軟、近晚洋商續在求出、據云産價微降、故順全隆有近期四元八角二分之西貢五百　拋出、 Also, it is reported that foreign rice softened slightly in the afternoon, and foreign merchants continued to seek sales in the late evening. A Quiet Bran Market

The bran market has been unusually quiet recently. Because foreign firms are inactive and large factories have accumulated bran, people are quiet and inactive. However, small factories' bran is selling relatively well in the mainland, so the market is stable. Currently, the prices of bran at various stalls are all quoted at 2 yuan and 7 jiao, with little difference.

Over 10,000 Pieces of Raw Sugar Offered in the Sugar Market

Yesterday, the sugar market trend was stable, but the transaction volume of domestic raw sugar suddenly increased significantly, because the sales channels have gradually been activated. The guild's negotiated prices were: 24 raw granulated white sugar spot goods at 18 yuan and 7 jiao and 5 fen, unchanged; re-export bonded warehouse goods at 5 yuan, 2 jiao and 3 fen, up 3 fen; 89 grade Dutch red sugar spot goods at 13 yuan and 9 jiao; Taikoo Sugar B mark at 19 yuan and 2 jiao and 5 fen, up 5 fen; this factory's first-grade refined white sugar at 18 yuan and 1 jiao. At the market opening, Guangdong merchants offered more than 4,000 boxes of sliced green sugar at 9 yuan each, and more than 500 units of strip green sugar at 9 yuan and 3 jiao each. Chaozhou merchants offered more than 6,000 bags of Chaozhou green sugar at 10 yuan and 5 jiao to 9 yuan and 6 jiao each. Because Ningbo and Wuxi merchants were actively buying in large quantities yesterday, and the land price in Shantou was reported to have risen, the market was enthusiastic and the transaction volume suddenly became lively.

Commercial News

Finance

A Wave of Bullish News Drives Speculation Up by $11.4

▲U.S. Government Considers Changing Silver Policy

The gold market had been repeatedly falling for days due to the wavering of the bullish front. Unexpectedly, yesterday, bullish news flooded the market, boosting buying interest and vigorous price increases. Sentiment remained strong. However, it weakened briefly due to a strengthening exchange rate. Early morning overseas silver markets showed flat prices in both England and America, while forward silver prices rose. Exchange rates fluctuated. London spot gold fell by 5.5 pence, but sentiment improved. This was due to reports in the Japanese press that the Central Bank was shipping a large quantity of gold bars for export, valued at £500,000, to be transferred to Hong Kong for exchange into silver. The reason was the recent extreme tightness of the silver market and lack of cash buyers, leading to unusually low reserves, which directly affected the gold market significantly. Now that the Central Bank has begun shipping large quantities for export, it will inevitably alleviate pressure in the market, and the silver market is expected to see some improvement. Speculators may not be overly embarrassed when settling their positions. Initial off-market bids were for $56.7, but few were willing to sell. Major firms like Hengyu, Futaiheng, and Dadecheng actively bought, quickly pushing the price up to $63. Hengchangyong and Yongli sold at the higher price. The Central Bank's official rates were announced, showing flat prices in England and America. The Customs Gold Unit further contracted by 6 li, and the standard speculative gold price retreated to.

Various rumors circulated regarding the Central Bank shipping 10,000 taels of cash and opening spot positions. Demand in the market exceeded supply, driving prices higher. However, because many were eager to sell at the high price and the exchange rate was stable, prices fluctuated and then declined. Banks showed a greater appetite for US dollars than British pounds, briefly pushing the price close to the $60 mark, but buying interest remained strong, allowing prices to rebound after the dip. The silver equalization tax remained unchanged at 6.25%. While the British exchange rate at 1 shilling 5.75 pence did not have a significant impact, major firms continued to buy. Prices then rallied again. However, due to the easing exchange rate and active supply from merchants, prices gradually fell. Major firms repeatedly sold heavily. Even those who were holding positions were forced to capitulate due to the rigid domestic market. The $60 mark could not be maintained, and bullish sentiment was shaken. The market weakened. However, because the initial rise had been too rapid and buying desires had not been fully satisfied, activity returned after the dip, and prices gradually recovered. At noon, the market appeared stable, fluctuating around the $60 level, as rumors circulated that the Central Bank was opening cash positions and importing gold bars. In the afternoon, the market immediately rose above $60. The rumors of cash opening intensified, and buyers flocked in. Western firms like 克萊 (Kèlái) also bought, causing a sudden surge. Sentiment improved further after the opening, and prices continued to rise. However, because major firms were dumping at the high price and banks were still selling, prices retreated. Due to the weakening exchange rate, buying interest remained strong. The initial reduction in Indian silver was three annas, and prices managed to hold after the dip. Later, a Reuters dispatch from Washington stated that, according to recent dispatches from Shanghai, the U.S. government might be willing to change its silver policy, reducing silver purchases and lowering the silver content of coins to alleviate the hardship suffered by China. This bullish news triggered another surge, but because supply remained abundant at the high price and the Western firm 克萊 (Kèlái) was also closing positions, and banks were selling, Indian silver rebounded by one anna a second time, gradually falling back. However, buying interest had not been extinguished, and the market closed strong. Throughout the day, demand exceeded supply, buying interest revived, and there were occasional dips. Bullish activity was also strong, leading to an optimistic trend. Below is a record of the day's market activity:

The morning opening was $961.5, a rebound of $6.2 from last Saturday. Dafayong, Hengyu, Yuankangxiang, Dadecheng, Tianfeng, and others bought bullion, driving prices up by $4.5 due to demand exceeding supply. Qianchangxiang, Qingyu, Shenkang, Yicheng, and Shunmao sold, causing prices to fall to $2.8. Hengyu, Yuankangxiang, and Yongfeng continued to buy, raising prices to $3.8. Hengxingyuan, Qingfayong, Dafayong, and Dadecheng sold again, pushing prices back to $1.9. 華比 (Huábǐ) bought February U.S. dollars at $34. Shunmao continued to buy, pulling prices up by $1. Hengyu bought and then sold, resulting in a flat price. At this time, the Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation's rates were announced, showing flat British rates and a U.S. dollar increase of .0625, causing market fluctuations. Dadecheng and Changda were forced to sell, pushing prices down to $1.1. Shunmao and Hengchangyong aggressively bought bullion, raising prices to $2.5. However, because 安達 (Āndá) and Mitsui were selling February shillings at 5.625, Qianchangxiang, Yongli, Yifengyong, Yuqingyong, Fuxingyong, and others sold, causing prices to fall to $.01. Dadecheng, Hengchangyong, and Qianchangxiang bought during the dip. Shanghai bought March U.S. dollars at $33.75, raising the price to $3. Hengyu, Dafayong, Huixiang, Dadecheng, and Hengxing sold, and prices retreated to $.07. Xingye bought February U.S. dollars at $34.0625. Zhaofengchang and Fuyu competed to buy, and retail investors rushed to cover positions, pushing prices up to $4. Hengyu, Yuanyi, Dadecheng, and Huilai sold, and prices gradually retreated to $.07. Hengyu, Tongtaichang, Dingkang, and Hengchangyong bought again, raising prices to $1.7. However, the exchange rate strengthened and then gradually softened. Dadecheng sold bullion continuously. Changda and Qianchangxiang also sold at the $60 mark, finally breaking it and falling to $59.2. Zhaofengchang and Futaiheng covered their positions during the dip, recovering to $60.05. Hengchangyong, Dadecheng, Huixiang, and Yongfeng sold, and prices gradually fell to $57.5. Fuyu, Yicheng, Zhaofengchang, Ruikang, Dingkang, Hengyu, and others successively bought, and rumors of the Central Bank opening cash positions circulated, recovering prices to $60.02. The noon close was $959.5, because Dadecheng and Fuxingyong slightly sold. After the close, Hengyu continued to buy, and prices were slightly stable.

The afternoon opening was $963.7, due to stronger rumors of the Central Bank opening cash positions. Shunli, Dadecheng, Hengyu, Dafayong, and Zhaofengchang bought again. 華比 (Huábǐ) bought February U.S. dollars at .0625, raising prices to $7. Qianchangxiang, Yuanyi, Yuanmaoyong, Yifengyong, and others sold at the higher price. Mitsui sold March shillings at 3.375, retreating to $4.5. At this time, Dafayong and Hengyu bought and then sold, struggling around $5. Hengyu, Dingkang, Yuqingyong, and Yongfeng bought again, and prices rose to $7.5. Fuxingyong, Yuanyi, Changda, and Tianfeng successively sold at the higher price, retreating to $5. Richang and others bought, while Changda sold. At this time, the initial report of Indian silver shrinking was 2.3 annas, and prices hovered around $6. The exchange rate showed signs of softening, March shillings were at 3.375. Chinese merchants wanted to close positions. Zhaofengchang, Dadecheng, Hengyu, Dingchang, Dingkang, and others continued to buy. A Reuters dispatch stated that the U.S. might reduce silver purchases or lower the silver content of coins, and prices rose again to $8.5. Shunli and Hengyu sold at the higher price, falling to $7.3. Hengxing and others continued to buy, raising prices to $8.8. Shunli, Dafayong, Tongfu, Yuanyi, and others sold. Guohuo Jiaotong released February U.S. dollars at $9.375. The Bank of England sold March shillings at 3.375. A second report of Indian silver came, rebounding by one anna, and prices fell to $5.5. Dadecheng and Qianchangxiang still had an appetite, and prices rose to $7.2. Zhentai and Hengyu sold to $6.2, but demand was very strong. The closing price was $966.7. After the close, prices continued to rise above $7.5. The highest price of the day was $968.8, and the lowest price was $957.95, a fluctuation of $11.3. The final result was a rebound of $11.4 from last Saturday.

The settlement price, based on the Central Bank's standard speculative gold price, fell again to $989.6, approximately $23 from the closing price, a decrease of more than $14 from last Saturday. The registered price for this month is $946, and for February, it is $960. The registered price for the afternoon market is $953 for this month and $969.9 for February. Additional water (补水) was $946 in the morning and $969 in the afternoon. Fine gold was $955.5, down $6. Spot goods remained scarce.

The selling price required an additional $2. Rumors were rampant regarding the Central Bank opening and importing spot goods, but they were not confirmed by spot dealers. It was feared that the clearing committee was covering short positions. However, it was widely rumored that the Central Bank had opened and imported a significant amount of speculative gold in both the morning and afternoon markets, totaling over 1,000 pieces, handled by Futaiheng, Dadecheng, Ruikang, and Fuchang. Some said they were collateral notes, but there were conflicting accounts. As of today, there were only 91 notes remaining for this month, excluding official notes.

Demand in the market exceeded supply. In summary, Futaiheng, Ruikang, Hengyu, Fuxing, Shunmao, Hengchangyong, Yuanchangyong, Yongfeng, Zhaofengchang, Dingkang, Chunyuanyong, Dadecheng, and others were on the buying side, while Hengyu, Fuxingyong, Huixiang, Dachangxiang, Yuanyi, Dafayong, Yifengyong, Changda, Yuanmaoyong, Changshengyong, Wanxing, Shunli, and others were on the selling side. Dadecheng, Qianchangxiang, and Hengxing first sold and then bought. Shunli and Yuanmaoyong first bought and then sold. The Dalian gang (大連帮) Wanxing traded a total of over 1,400 pieces, netting out over 500 pieces. Shunli traded a total of over 1,000 pieces, netting out less than 200. The Guangdong gang (廣帮) Shengshengda had mixed buying and selling. Hengxing bought and sold over 100 pieces each. The total trading volume for the day was 44,338 pieces in the morning market and 30,723 pieces in the afternoon market. February contracts totaled 24,507 pieces. There were a total of 58 long positions and 58 short positions.

Yesterday, the official notes were closed out by the short side, Yingfenghong, for 14 pieces. Today, the long side, Yongfenghong and Hengyu, will each take in 7 pieces. The settlement price was $946.

Chinese Merchants' Appetite is Healthy

Foreign Exchange Loosens and then Tightens

According to yesterday's foreign dispatches, London long-term bills and New York silver prices remained unchanged. The Montreux forward silver price was flat and rose 4.5 li. London spot gold fell 5.5 pence. The British exchange rate against the U.S. shrank by one-half, while the U.S. rate against the British rose by .25. The British rate against the French was unchanged, while the U.S. rate against the French fell .375. The foreign exchange market opened in the morning with near-term selling prices of 1 shilling 5.0625 pence for British pounds and $34.9375 for U.S. dollars, showing no significant changes compared to last Saturday. The Central Bank's official rates were announced, showing flat prices in England and America, with the Customs Gold Unit falling by 6 li. However, the psychology of Chinese merchants was boosted by the news that the Central Bank was shipping cash for export. Although the process after the opening was tight, it was minimal. Banks showed a greater appetite for US dollars than British pounds, and the overall trend was mediocre. The Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation's official rates were announced, showing flat British rates and a U.S. dollar increase of .0625. The market was extremely volatile until the silver equalization tax was announced unchanged. However, because the psychology of Chinese merchants remained good, the market was able to maintain. Afterwards, the banks' appetite remained strong, and the Chinese merchants' appetite turned sluggish. The process gradually became loose. The market tightened again in the afternoon due to rumors of positive developments. However, banks continued to sell at the higher price, causing some fluctuations. The initial report of Indian silver shrinking was 3 annas, and the psychology of Chinese merchants remained strong. In addition, a Reuters dispatch reported that the U.S. was reducing silver purchases and lowering the silver content of coins, and the process remained tight. Later, because banks were still selling, Indian silver rebounded by one anna and prices were slightly flat. The closing near-term selling prices were 1 shilling 4.875 pence for British pounds and $34.6875 for U.S. dollars, showing a tightening of 1.5625 for British pounds and .25 for U.S. dollars compared to last Saturday. Chinese merchants slightly bought over 300,000 shillings and U.S. dollars. The Xinfeng 洋行 (Yángháng) and the 美東 (Měidōng) Bank also bought. Below is a record of the day's transactions:

Call Loans Have Significantly Eased

Based on an observation of the situation of Chinese and foreign banks in the market at the beginning of the week yesterday, it seems that there is a possibility of returning to the original state. Yesterday, the foreign call loan rate in the market had eased significantly, with the same price as the previous Sunday at 4 jiao 8 fen. There was also a significant easing of the call loan rate in the morning and at noon, with the initial rate being 2 jiao 5 fen, and then only 1 jiao 8 fen. In terms of call loan transactions, there were over 2.8 million in morning transfers, over 1.2 million in new transactions, over 400,000 in noon transactions, and over 800,000 in transactions at the small clearing house. In terms of banknote transactions, over 800,000 was recovered, over 1.2 million in new banknotes were issued into circulation, and over 600,000 in marked banknotes. In terms of foreign collateral transactions, over 800,000 was redeemed, over 1.3 million was newly made, customers contributed 300,000, and 500,000 went to the bank. Bank collections and settlements included 2.67 million in foreign bank collections and settlements, 5.23 million in various goods, foreign exchange collateral, and miscellaneous collections, 1.2 million in foreign exchange settlement payments, 800,000 in special exchange payments, and 500,000 in warehousing. Chinese bank collections and settlements included 3.1 million in collections and settlements, 6.45 million in various goods, foreign exchange collateral, tax, and miscellaneous collections, 900,000 in special exchange payments, 900,000 in foreign exchange settlement payments, and 600,000 in warehousing. Japanese bank collections and settlements included 2.5 million in collections and settlements, 5.89 million in various goods, foreign exchange collateral, and miscellaneous collections, 900,000 in foreign exchange settlement payments, 800,000 in special exchange payments, and 400,000 in warehousing. Money shops (錢莊) 洋公單 (yánggōngdān) collections and settlements totaled over 42 million, call loan collections and settlements over 5.8 million, various remittance collections over 600,000, and cash receipts over 4-500,000. In addition, the total exchange volume at the bill exchange yesterday was 11,165,697.7 yuan, including 6,493,261.3 yuan in silver dollars and 5,158,436.4 yuan in silver exchange settlements. The interest rate on official collateral loans was 2 jiao 4 fen per 1,000 yuan per day, and the discount rate on official collateral was 2 jiao 9 fen per 1,000 yuan per day.

Rumors Dissipate, Bond Market Reverses

丨Three to Six Jiao Better Than Saturday丨

Yesterday, the Chinese Stock Exchange market seemed to have improved slightly. The unfounded rumors that had been circulating were confirmed to be completely false, and foreign call loans had also eased somewhat. Market sentiment was stable, and many short positions that had been accumulated over several days were gradually being covered, along with some arbitrage transactions. As a result, sentiment turned bullish, and the trend appeared strong. If foreign call loans continue to ease, there is hope for improvement in market prices. Throughout yesterday, the opening in the morning was due to the foreign call loan rate only being quoted at 4 jiao 8 fen, a retreat of 7 fen from the previous day. Sentiment turned stable, and the rumors that had been circulating on Saturday were confirmed to be unfounded. Scattered buying and swap transactions were not quiet. The 編遣 (biānqiǎn) bonds immediately rose by 4 jiao 5 fen, and the 裁兵 (cáibīng) bonds rose by half a yuan. The trend remained strong throughout. Although the 北帮 (Běibāng) sold, the market price was not suppressed. Afterwards, the 23rd issue rose by more than 6 jiao 5 fen. In the second session, some long positions were slightly closed out, and another round of arbitrage began. Although selling in the 11th issue surged, the market price still slowly rose. The back issues, such as the 整六 (zhěngliù), showed signs of weakness. Under normal circumstances, a rebound could have been expected in the afternoon. However, the call loan rate in the afternoon was only 2 jiao 8 fen, a rapid decline compared to before. Sentiment revived again. The 裁兵 (cáibīng) bonds continued to rise by 3 jiao, and the back issues also improved slightly. At the close, the temporary long positions on the floor were slightly closed out, retreating slightly by about 5 fen or 1 jiao. Afterwards, the 47th issue was actively bought in the afternoon, rising sharply by 3 jiao. The trend was strong and stable. Even if it does not continue to rise, it will fluctuate for a while. In summary, the result of the day's market prices was that they were 3 to 6 or 7 jiao higher than Saturday. The total transaction volume was 13,200,500 yuan, and 10 shares of stock. Raw Cotton Speculative Yarn Fluctuates Normally

The yarn market is calm. Overseas cotton markets are trending downward, and sentiment has declined slightly. However, the large holdings of the Tongji and Tongcheng companies remain unchanged, and the market has not seen significant changes. Sales of spot yarn can still be maintained.

Gold Rooster Nearly Stable, Far Off Declines

Before the opening of the raw cotton speculative yarn market, it was expected that there would be a price decline, as foreign cotton had fallen sharply, with near-term declines of 3-4 jiao and far-term declines of 5-6 jiao. By the second or third round of auctions, rumors were rampant in the market, saying that representatives from Chinese yarn factories were very busy. Another rumor said that a meeting was being held somewhere, with a proposal to reduce production in yarn factories. However, a thorough investigation by the reporter found that there was no need to stop or reduce production. Although one factory had stopped production, it was due to internal reasons or organizational restructuring. Market prices rose slightly as a result. The result was that the current month rose by 4 jiao, March rose by 1 jiao, and the other months fell by 3-4 jiao. In the afternoon, it was heard that purchasing of spot yarn by the Hunan and Guangdong gangs was still smooth, and market sentiment was slightly calm. All months rose by 1-2-3 jiao. Sales included 950 bales from Dafeng, 750 bales from Yuanda, 550 bales from Ruida, 350 bales from Zhenda, 500 bales from Yicheng, 700 bales from Runkang, 350 bales from Jifeng, 500 bales from Tongji, 400 bales from Shenji, 750 bales from Yuanyi, 700 bales from Changfeng, and 1,950 bales from Gengfeng. Speculative Raw Cotton with Reduced Production in the Air

The cotton market declined slightly. Indian cotton continued to fall, and the situation took a sharp turn for the worse. American cotton was also weak, and sentiment became softer. Talk of yarn factories reducing production became more intense, and the market was even harder to stabilize. However, Tongcheng continued to buy more during the dips, and the speculative gold price

is slightly higher. New sellers are not seen to be active.

Speculative Zheng Cotton Declines Slightly

Before the opening of the speculative raw cotton market, most people expected a decline of several jiao, as American cotton was trending downward, and the decline in Indian cotton was accelerating, causing weakness in sentiment. Rumors of yarn factories stopping production resurfaced. However, new sellers were not active in the market. In fact, when Indian cotton had risen step by step the day before, the speculative raw cotton market was also calm and did not follow the rise, so there were not many floating long positions on the floor that were eager to close out. Women Not Allowed to Flirt

— Impotent

["Of the myriad remaining, not even a sliver remains. I've rarely seen such a delightful woman. My eyes are dazzled, my words fail me, my soul flies away for half a day."]

These are Zhang Junrui's first words upon seeing Yingying in the "Amazing Encounter" scene of the Romance of the Western Chamber. I think at that time, Yingying was in mourning attire and didn't particularly dress up in a "delicately charming" manner. Yet, this Mr. Zhang Junrui was so captivated at first sight that he was utterly infatuated and obsessed. Zhang was truly a hungry ghost for beauty. If Cui Yingying had donned gorgeous clothes, applied rouge and powder, and dressed like those "promiscuous young ladies" who frequent hotels and game halls, I wonder how Mr. Zhang Junrui would have been "possessed" upon seeing her? No, Zhang Junrui would definitely turn his head away and leave such a woman, and the events that followed wouldn't have occurred. The Romance of the Western Chamber wouldn't have been able to continue.

My mind is also very stubborn, and my tolerance is quite narrow, unlike some places where if the mistress of the house goes out as a guest or shopping and no one follows her, the black lacquer bench becomes very unhappy and looks down on her. In the past, when my yellow-faced wife went out, even though she didn't wear any strange or gorgeous clothes, she always put on some rouge and powder, and I was very dissatisfied. Once, when the mistress of the house went out, she naturally did as usual, and I was so annoyed that I questioned her. ["You usually don't put on rouge and powder at home, but you must put on rouge and powder when you go out. What's the reason for that? If you put on some powder at home, that's understandable, but if you must put on rouge and powder when you go out, it's simply of questionable intent."] My yellow-faced wife was truly speechless after being questioned by me, and she smiled and said, ["If I go out looking disheveled, it doesn't seem appropriate. What's the reasoning behind that? I won't apply rouge and powder when I go out anymore." I think to myself, my views are not in line with modern trends, but I'm confident that my reasoning isn't bad.]

According to a news report, ["The Public Security Bureau of Ping City, acting on the instructions of the municipal government, reported that a citizen, Chen Shaowang, stated that recently, there have been some women who engage in the trick of seducing young men in public places all day long. Please take measures to ban them," etc.] Indeed, all young men are in the midst of sexual urges, so how can they withstand the temptation of charming and beautiful women? However, according to Chen Shaowang, these are mostly women without occupations who make a living by engaging in prostitution, or women who pretend to be students while secretly flaunting their youth. One type of woman is driven by economic pressure, while the other is driven by sexual desire. I think that for those who are forced to resort to flirting due to economic pressure, there may be some justification. As for those in academic circles who are said to be like secret prostitutes, they must be a very small number of bad elements, and it's definitely not a widespread phenomenon.

However, I deeply observe that in society, those who wear flamboyant clothes and flirt are not limited to the above two types of people. Whether from prominent families or small households, whether grandmothers or young ladies, I dare not say they're all flirting, but their strange and gorgeous clothes attract onlookers, and there's reliable evidence for this. I ask, what are their motivations? I dare not make wild guesses. Even in terms of material things, the losses are countless. Not to mention rouge, face powder, lipstick, etc., even in terms of clothing, they must be changed every six months. What's long in the first half of the year becomes short in the second half of the year, what's big in the second half of the year becomes small in the first half of the year, and whatever silk is popular now, they'll make something out of that silk, and in another six months, they'll make something out of another silk. I ask, how can this account be calculated?

Or some may say that it's understandable for young ladies to do this, but what is the purpose of grandmothers doing it? According to those who understand women's psychology, men often like women who are flirtatious and attract attention, so they use flamboyant means to win over their husbands as a way to resist inferior goods. Whether these words are true or not, I still have some doubts.

Wine and Women

— Hui

The wine in Zhu Lao San's stomach was generating a fire-like heat. His face flushed crimson, and his nerves were in disarray. In his memory, in his fiery red eyes, there was only that woman, the woman living on the second floor.

Madly, he muttered to himself, yelling and cursing. Suddenly, he cried, but when he was crying fiercely, he suddenly laughed again. He told stories to the person sitting in front of him, and he cursed at the person sitting in front of him. Although when he was making too much noise, the guard standing outside the wooden fence would impatiently open the door, using great force to strike him with the bamboo whip in his hand, cursing him harshly. But to Zhu Lao San, who was spewing the smell of wine from his mouth, it didn't seem to matter. He didn't know that there was a fierce god standing in front of him, scolding him and wielding a thick bamboo whip, that his hands and feet were shackled with iron rings, and that all around him were thick wooden bars. He didn't know the lack of freedom and the pain inflicted on him. He continued to yell, curse, laugh, and cry. In his mind, he had no idea that this was a place where there was absolutely no freedom, where absolutely no one could be free. His clamor was something that a person who had lost their freedom wouldn't have.

The time had reached dusk, and the sky was a somber black. The faces of the people inside the wooden fence were blurred and hard to see. The guard standing outside the gate was also impatiently waving the bamboo whip in his hand, pacing back and forth with heavy steps, the sound of his leather shoes clanging.

One hundred, two hundred pairs of eyes flickered beside the wooden fence. These flickering eyes naturally focused on the guard walking back and forth, as if telling him: ["It's getting late, and we're all still hungry!"] But it was all in vain. The guard who was pacing and smoking a cigarette didn't seem to notice at all. He just kept reaching into his pocket to take out his watch, checking to see if it was time for his shift to change. He didn't pay any attention to the hungry eyes focused on him.

At this time, Zhu Lao San felt that his head weighed a thousand pounds. Drowsy, his vision went black, and he fell to the floor without knowing anything. He fell asleep just like that on the hard floor.

The north wind whistled in from outside the wooden fence. Zhu Lao San felt a chill all over his body and woke up from his drunken dream. When he opened his eyes, he was very strange and very scared. What on earth was this place? Why did he come here and lie down on the floor to sleep?

His nerves gradually cleared, and his eyes kept looking around under the dim light. He remembered very clearly that he had been eating and drinking in a restaurant at noon today. Why? Why did he end up lying here tonight? This was definitely not the place he wanted to come to!

At this time, Zhu Lao San wanted to stand up, but he realized that his hands and feet were shackled with iron rings. He understood in his heart that he must have committed some crime. At this time, he could only sit there blankly thinking, recalling what had happened after lunch today.

In the afternoon, after Zhu Lao San finished lunch, he walked home from the restaurant. He had drunk too much wine, and he always staggered when he walked. When he got home, he didn't know why, but he ran up to the second floor to Mrs. Wang's room. He went mad, he went to hug her, to caress her, to [censored]. But Mrs. Wang cried out. He was vaguely caught by the people who broke into the room from outside, and after that, he didn't know anything.

Zhu Lao San tried hard to recall again, but he couldn't remember what happened after he was caught. He thought, he looked at his clothes. At this time, he realized that his clothes were torn, and there was a faint pain on his back and legs. Only then did he begin to understand what had happened to him today, all because of wine and women.

The gloomy shadows of the night were deeply imprinted on the ground outside the wooden fence. There was no light at all, only the piercing wind was blowing, sending cold air to the people inside the wooden fence. Looking at the pitch-black sky, it looked like it was about to rain. At this time, Zhu Lao San sank into recollection.

Two Yellow Comic Exhibition

— Yi Min

Comics have indeed become popular in China recently, and in the art of painting, comics do occupy a considerable position. Moreover, the power of comics may be greater than that of general pictures. They can satirize society, inspire thought, and everything else is perhaps beyond the reach of purely aesthetic pictures.

Because comics themselves have a kind of humorous tone, they are often regarded by some people as clowns on the stage and are overlooked. In fact, a comic has the potential to make you cry, laugh, feel sentimental, and sympathize! Therefore, I think the comic exhibition in Shanghai, although it is the first time it has been held, is worth visiting.

Stepping onto the fourth floor of the Continental Shopping Mall, turning a corner from the elevator is the first room of the comic exhibition, which is entirely the work of Huang Shiying, with a total of sixty-four works. The four walls are hung full of exhibits, truly a feast for the eyes!

We acknowledge that comics, like newspapers, are a mirror that reflects society. In a fragmented society like China, the society reflected in comics is, of course, also fragmented, and comic artists are, of course, dissatisfied with society. Therefore, among the sixty-four works, many can be found that reflect the fragmented state of society.

[Taking Risks], [Plowing on an Empty Stomach], [The Fate of the Poor], [The Hunger Riot], [Unemployment], [Refugees], [The Cry of Life], [Inspection of Disaster Areas], [Crying from Hunger and Cold]—don't these works depict the bankruptcy of Chinese villages and the economic downturn of cities? [The Landlord's Tour], [The Decline of a Large Family], [Illegitimate Child], [Brothel Mother's Whip], [Discovery of a Woman's Photo], [After Being Full]—several works have also depicted the current Chinese society, the old ethics, and various contradictions. [The Colonial Tide], [The Roar of the Oppressed People]—these works depict the suffering of oppressed people under the iron heel of imperialism. When we see [The Night of the Great Wall], we will think of the lost territory in Northeast China. When we see [Ronin], we will think of the activities of Japanese ronin in Shanghai during the January 28th Incident. Here, it is enough for us to experience the potential in these works. The author further uses his keen thinking and humorous style to do his best to satirize and guide society and the country.

Arriving in the second room, the seventy-four comics here are entirely the work of Huang Ding. In Huang Ding's works, there are naturally many that expose the fragmented state of Chinese society. [The Ordeal of Debt Evaders], [Debt Collection], [The Landlord is Coming], [Difficulty Eating], [Hungry People Shouting Outside the Window], [Country People Being Fooled]—these works depict the bankruptcy of rural and urban areas and the downturn of the economy even more completely. In addition, there are as many as eighteen sketches in the entire collection, with street scenes, scenery, and portraits as the main themes. In addition, [Imperialism in Zhong,

[Concession Combination Line], etc., are several comics that powerfully arouse national spirit.

Looking at the comics of Huang Shiying and Huang Ding, their composition and brushwork each have their own style, and all of their works are skilled and content are worthy of being called above the standard. Finally, I hope that this comic exhibition will call attention to cartoonists across the country.

Pawned, Awaiting Redemption

— Prison City

When I was studying, I didn't understand what pawnshops were all about. But in recent years, the pawnshops that are lined up in Shanghai are very familiar. Because the number of times I and my poor friends have gone to pawnshops has increased day by day, and seeing the number of unemployed and impoverished people in society increasing day by day, I thought that the business of pawnshops should be better. But recently

Impressions of Reading the Newspaper

— Hong

Correction: Yesterday's drawing omitted the title [Starting Over]

Page 17

Recently, I have seen several pawnshop doors with red paper and black characters, which are particularly eye-catching: [Pawned, Awaiting Redemption]. Moreover, they are mostly large and very famous pawnshops, which makes people feel suspicious. When I asked a more knowledgeable friend, he laughed at me for being ignorant and strange, and said that the situation was more than that. Once, they almost all closed down completely! This made me even more stunned. The reason is that there are really more and more people going to pawnshops, but pawning without redeeming is the fatal wound of pawnshops. Therefore, they have to [Pawned, Awaiting Redemption], and the reason is here. Although pawnshops like more people to pawn things and the business is more lively, their main purpose is to seek high profits. If I pawn something worth ten dollars, they will charge me one dollar in interest in just six months. If I can redeem it, this kind of business can prosper. If I can't redeem it and it's left as inventory, the boss's capital can't circulate in the current widespread economic downturn and the phenomenon of prices falling day by day, and there's no way out.

From this small phenomenon, we can see more clearly! People's poverty is becoming more and more profound. Especially in the prosperity of big cities, it reveals its latent crisis even more. Now everything is being pawned due to the decline of the pawnshop industry's [Pawned, Awaiting Redemption], and the price of pawns is still increasing, but there are still more people going to pawnshops, but it can be imagined that it is even more impoverished situation, since they pawn more and get less money, and have no power to redeem it? Otherwise, it would never be willing to sacrifice high-priced goods and be unwilling to buy them out at a low price.

Ms. Wang Bingmei Tang Poetry

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Listening to An Wanshan's Bili Song Li Qi

Cut bamboo from the Southern Mountain for the bili, This music originally came from Kucha,

Flowing through the Han land, the tune turns strange, A Cool Prefecture barbarian plays it for me.

Neighbors who hear it often sigh; Distant travelers thinking of home all shed tears.

The world understands listening but doesn't understand appreciating, In the long hall, it comes and goes by itself in the wind.

The dry mulberry and old cypress are cold and soughing, Nine Phoenixes sing in a chaotic chirp.

Dragon roars and tiger howls erupt at once; Ten thousand sounds and a hundred springs meet autumn together.

Suddenly it changes to Yuyang's interjection, Yellow clouds are bleak and the sun is dark;

The changed tune is like hearing the spring of willows, The Fan flowers in the upper forest shine with new eyes.

On New Year's Eve, high halls are lined with bright candles, A cup of fine wine, a song.
