Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

A Brief History of Film Development (2)

— Wen Ying

(2) Leland Stanford's Production of Linked Films

Many years ago, there was a Griffith (D.W. Griffith), who was originally an actor in vaudeville. He suddenly set up a very simple small film studio in New York and began shooting moving pictures. His speed of production was truly astonishing, producing approximately one film per week. Later, he ran to New Jersey and filmed many wilderness westerns. Because he did not have much money and hired mostly extras, the actors he used had to play several roles in one film, being used three or four times a day to make it count. Therefore, the Indians attacked by cowboys were often played by those who played the cowboys, and the Indian woman sitting in front of the bonfire, only seen from the back, was probably Griffith's own wife or a friend of his wife.

At that time, Griffith had no idea that his talent would later become world-renowned, shining globally in such blockbusters as (Birth of a Nation). How could he have foreseen that the girl he hired, earning three dollars a day, would later become "America's Sweetheart" and is now a Hollywood social leader, Mary Pickford? One day, Mary Pickford led two apprehensive girls to the film studio and asked Griffith to give them some work to do as well. At the time, Griffith did not anticipate that one of them would later become one of the greatest film actors of her generation, the protagonist of famous films such as "Two Orphans," Lillian Gish. In Griffith's eyes at that time, he could not see what was so great about Mary Pickford and Lillian Gish. To him, they were just some lively and active girls.

Returning to matters before Griffith, we can mention Leland Stanford. He unintentionally laid the foundation for one of America's six largest enterprises, but he did not know it. One evening after a banquet, he brought up a theory that a horse's four hooves are simultaneously off the ground when running at top speed. This statement does not seem strange to us today, because we have seen it many times in sports films or war films. But at that time, one of the guests present did not believe his theory. So Stanford argued with that person. Neither would give way, and they finally made a bet. Stanford wanted to prove that his theory was correct in order to win the bet. Unwittingly, this led to the beginning of moving pictures.

Stanford was a wealthy man. He was also an athlete skilled in horsemanship. Having made a bet with a friend, he devoted himself to winning it. He wanted to use photography to prove his idea, but after taking photos for many years, the results were not very satisfactory. Finally, he met a photographer named John D. Isaacs, who gave him an idea that could prove his theory, but could also show that his theory was wrong. He told Stanford to place dozens of cameras in a row on the ground, and use a kind of electrical mechanism to make the fast horse walk past the front of the camera boxes, with many camera boxes opening the lens covers in sequence, capturing the real situation on the ground one by one. The result of this experiment was a row of linked photographs, and the different positions of the horse's hooves were clearly visible.

Stanford examined each of the photos and knew that his theory was correct. He showed them to his friend and received the wagered money. In 1882, he published a book about the entire affair, and the money for printing the book was also the money won from the bet. After that, he forgot all about it. But these photographs were the first motion pictures, the first photographs to show the motion of an object. If it were not for that bet, perhaps we would not be able to see Clark Gable or Marlene Dietrich today. Isn't this a very strange industrial anecdote? Of course, Stanford did not know that he had invented something new. After his book was published, the minds of many inventors were spurred by his experiment and began to work frantically. They felt that the method of photographing with many linked camera boxes was not enough. They began to think about using one camera box to continuously shoot multiple films. At this time, the great inventor Edison also felt a peculiar interest in this matter. (To be continued)

Audience Opinion

Review of [The Big Road]

— Lü Yi

The life of workers is painful and monotonous. The author of [The Big Road] uses two young girls to adjust their lives, encourage them, make them forget the hardships of work, and make their spirits active. This is indeed very ideal. But the poet's ideal is always beautiful. Every scene and every shot here is full of poetic sentiment and the emotion of painting. Poetry and painting weave the picture.

The first half of the drama's tone is light, and then gradually becomes tense as the story progresses. Until Jin Ge and others are imprisoned and beaten, the atmosphere on the screen and in the sound is very tight and oppressive, which is indeed a successful effect.

The author's clear division of each character's personality is also not to be ignored. Jin Ge's intelligence and bravery, Lao Zhang's silence and suspicion, Zhang Da's recklessness and straightforwardness, Xiao Liu Zi's weakness and incompetence, and Zheng Jun's intellectual class style are all appropriately expressed, without any contradiction or excessiveness. The music accompanying the drama's relaxation is very appropriate and harmonious, which also helps a lot with the drama's appeal.

My Review of [The Big Road]

— Xiao Bai

The subject matter and significance of [The Big Road] show the importance of our country's current construction work, and also demonstrate the greatness of the masses' united strength. Although, under the interlocking oppression of imperialism and evil forces, heavy obstacles are used to hinder the work of the big road, it is finally overcome and ultimately successful because of the efforts of the masses themselves, their strong fighting spirit, and their indomitable courage.

However, I feel that there is still room for discussion, that is, whether this is an accurate portrayal of reality? The road workers' rejection of bribes and willingness to be tortured, the attitude of calmly facing death, and Li Lili and Chen Yanyan's resourcefulness and bravery in using the "beauty trap," are these real facts in the world? It makes people somewhat doubtful.

In this film, we hear the two tragic and passionate songs "[Road Opener]" and "[The Big Road]," which completely ignite the inner blood. Everything is a bright, cheerful, and energetic manifestation. Although the work only has sincere and earnest expectations, and has not yet earnestly sought the light of the future, its spirit is commendable enough.

"The Merry Widow" starring Jeanette MacDonald and Maurice Chevalier (today is the last day for this film to be screened)

Impressions After Seeing [The Big Road]

— Yu Bi

I think [The Big Road] is a film that contains excitement from beginning to end.

The director's efforts can be seen in every scene, light and powerful, such as Dingxiang kneading dough while moving her feet in time with the rhythm of [The Big Road Song]. Another example is the scene when Han Xiaoliuzi is arrested for stealing beef, Molly putting corn silk in her mouth, and the liveliness of Dingxiang and Molly. Intense scenes such as the road workers being beaten by the foreman, Jin Ge's conflict with the foreman, Dingxiang and Molly using the "beauty trap," the drunken Hufu, Jin Ge cutting the rope with scissors on the ground, and using his toes to pick up the scissors are all the most tense and clever places in the entire film for the director. The lyrics of several songs also help to make the entire film wonderful.

Some of the director's techniques seem to adopt those of [Song of the Fishermen], such as using the lyrics of the songs to perform the mood in the scenes. [The Big Road Song], [Road Opener], [Fengyang Song], and [Song of the Fishermen] are somewhat similar. The director handled the entire film lightly, tensely, and even humorously. However, the director's handling of several extras in the performance is not very powerful.

Actors such as Zhang Yi's silent and resolute performance, Jin Yan's cheerful performance, and Han Langen's playful performance are all successful. Chen Yanyan is indeed lovable, but in the last section when she goes to report, her gait is not tight enough, and her face also lacks a tense expression. Shang Guanwu and Zhang Zhizhi are quite good. Zheng Junli is competent, and the other actors are also quite hardworking.

The dubbing is very good. The photography is clear.

Anecdotes from [Rebirth Flower]

— Huo

△... Hu Die plays two roles in [Rebirth Flower]: Da Bao is a pitiful poor woman, and Er Bao is a noble lady. Hu Die has achieved a mastery of perfection in portraying the opposite expressions of this poverty and wealth. And the most difficult expression to perform is the transition from a sad face to a smiling face, and then from a smiling face back to a sad face. This was often seen during the filming of [Rebirth Flower].

△... Xuan Jinglin can be considered the most hardworking person in [Rebirth Flower]. This old mother usually sits in the film studio, and she doesn't care about the noise in the studio at all, as if she is sitting in another world, constantly whispering with director Zheng Zhengqiu about the expression of each shot. She is so hardworking, it is no wonder that she is praised by the vast audience.

△... In order to make the plot of [Rebirth Flower] more realistic, Zheng Xiaoqiu and Mei Xi were whipped all over their bodies with the warlord's leather whip until they turned purple, and this sacrifice obviously had great gains and great value, didn't it? The most touching scene in [Rebirth Flower] is this scene.

▲... Audiences who have seen [Twin Sisters] probably know that Er Bao (played by Hu Die) had a lover before marrying Commander Qian. That lover was a progressive revolutionary youth. In [Rebirth Flower], it will tell you the life of this youth.

▲... In [Twin Sisters], Da Bao was arrested and imprisoned for killing Commander Qian's sister. The next day, Da Bao's mother went to visit her in prison and learned that the prison officer Zhao De was Zhao Da, and his wife Jianying was Er Bao. As a result, Er Bao was moved by great ethics and forcibly took Da Bao out of prison. This is still the plot of [Twin Sisters]. What happens afterwards? Please see the currently released [Rebirth Flower] (but)

Film Novel

Policeman Rides the Dragon (White Lies) (4)

— Xin Zhi

Oliver nodded, indicating that he could take the phone. Mitchell then grabbed the telephone receiver. He heard his secretary's voice saying, "Captain Taylor is outside and wants to see you." Mitchell heard this and couldn't remember who Taylor was for a moment. After thinking for a while, he remembered that it was the bold policeman who had now been promoted to captain. He had come at just the right time, and he couldn't help but feel refreshed. He then pretended to be nonchalant and said, "Tell him to wait. I'm very busy. I'll ring the bell when I want to see him." After saying that, he hung up the phone. Oliver shouted, "Put your hands on the table, or I'll shoot." They then stared at each other in a daze. After a while, Mitchell pointed to the cigarette box on his desk and asked Oliver if he smoked. While Oliver was paying attention, and accidentally not on guard, Mitchell gently raised one leg and used his knee to press the electric bell under the table. A second later, a fully armed young police officer jumped in. He was tall, broad-shouldered, and had piercing eyes. When Joan saw him, her heart couldn't help but flutter. It turned out that this was Taylor Camden. When Oliver saw a police officer running in, he immediately became uneasy. But Camden calmly said to him, "Why don't you put down that gun? Aren't you just adding to your crimes?" As he spoke, he put one hand on Oliver's hand holding the gun and effortlessly snatched the gun away. Oliver helplessly fell into the chair and cried miserably.

At this time, Mitchell suddenly forgot about them, and suddenly regained his original identity as a fierce news reporter. He shouted loudly, "Hend! Roberts! Call the printing room! Tell them to stop working! Tell them to take off the cover and replace it with a new one! 'Attempted Murder in the Newsroom!' This is the biggest news of the year!" The entire newspaper office immediately went crazy with busyness. In the midst of everyone's busyness, Joan looked at Camden with affection and said, "Don't blame my dad. He's always like this." Mitchell said to Camden distractedly, "You're really something. That was really fun. Please come and see me when you have time, or I won't be so busy. You should know that today's events are the best news." As he said this, he reached out to grab the phone. Joan seized the opportunity and said, "I think, Dad, we should at least invite Captain Camden to dinner." When Camden heard this, he was overjoyed and kept spinning a hat in his hands. Mitchell said, "Of course. Of course. You take care of it." Joan then said to Camden, "Okay, Captain? How about tomorrow night?" Camden shook the hand Joan offered him and replied, "Tomorrow night." Joan added, "Seven o'clock. No need to wear a tuxedo." Camden said goodbye to everyone and left.

The next evening, Camden ran to Mitchell's country villa to attend Joan's invitation. But when he got there, he felt extremely uncomfortable. He had originally wanted to use this opportunity to get closer to Joan by coming to dinner. But he was not the only one invited that day, there were also many other male guests, all of whom he did not know. He rarely saw Joan during the meal. Later, Mitchell insisted on introducing him to the public, calling her the hero of his newsroom. This made him even more embarrassed. Later, he saw Joan talking to Axel Brantley. They were talking in very low voices, their attitude was extremely intimate, and he also heard that they had already been engaged. This made him feel even more uninterested. He suddenly realized that there was no point in lingering in this place. This was not his place, a policeman mixing among a group of playboys. From the beginning, he should have declined. He thought he would first go to the garden for a walk, smoke a cigarette, and then say goodbye to the host and go back. The garden was particularly quiet, and Camden walked alone in it. He laughed at himself for how suddenly arresting Mitchell had caused such a small disturbance in his life. As he was thinking, he suddenly heard a rustling sound behind him, followed by some weight like moonlight being added to his shoulders, followed by a delicate voice saying, "What's wrong with you? Why are you always avoiding me at night?" (To be continued)

Shen Bao Architecture Weekly

Progress of Domestic Building Materials in Recent Years (Part 1)

— Xue Cixin

Since the Yellow Emperor built palaces and houses, initiating the beginnings of architecture, and by the Zhou Dynasty, the scale of architecture was roughly established, progressing through the Han, Tang, Song, and Ming dynasties, with each era advancing in architecture. At that time, due to the limited uses of buildings, mostly confined to palaces, temples, and residences, the materials used were primarily bricks, stones, and timber. Unlike today's theaters, dance halls, apartments, and factories, which either prioritize practicality or aesthetics, it is insufficient to meet the needs without utilizing various materials. Therefore, the building materials of that era, sourced domestically, were sufficient and did not require foreign reliance. After the opening of maritime trade, European and American construction methods were introduced to our country. Thus, in terms of structure, there were steel frame projects and reinforced concrete buildings, and in terms of decoration, there were marble wall panels, mosaics, and patterned wooden floors. Other items such as door locks, hinges, glass, and paint relied solely on foreign goods. Even for something as small as a nail, domestic supply could not be fully depended upon. Lofty buildings and mansions in metropolitan areas are one thing, but even in remote rural areas, traces of foreign building materials are as rare as phoenix feathers. Observing this, it is clear that we should urgently catch up in improving and promoting domestic building materials. In recent years, the call for promoting domestic goods has spread throughout the country. Although in heavy industry, due to various economic and talent-related factors, there has not been significant progress, the advancement of practical domestic goods has shown a soaring trend. As the message spreads, existing domestic building materials are visibly improving, and those that did not exist are gradually being imitated or trial-produced. Although it is not possible to completely drive foreign goods out of the market at once, it is sufficient to replace them. If the people of the country can cherish this industry and promote the manufactured materials, then the future of domestic building materials will be limitless. Currently, there are already many types of domestic building materials, and we will discuss and analyze those that have shown improvement or achieved success in their development.

(1) Bricks and Tiles: In the past, brick and tile manufacturing mostly used earth kilns, using wooden molds to make blanks during agricultural off-seasons, which were then fired in earth kilns. Because of this, the sizes of bricks and tiles varied across regions, and the quality of materials also differed. Furthermore, workers were scattered among farmers, and kiln firing adhered rigidly to old methods, resulting in a daily decline in material quality. Industrial operators, due to the low profit margin, did not pay much attention to this. Until the prosperous era of exchanges in the early Republic, construction flourished, and this industry began to attract social attention. Initially, larger-scale brick and tile companies were organized, and new-style brick kilns were used. Some even used iron molds for making blanks. Therefore, in recent years, bricks and tiles have gradually improved, especially with the increasing thickness and length of brick blanks, reaching ten inches, which is commendable. The method and firing of tiles have also improved, and those who sell and use tiles have gradually learned to use the absorption rate of tiles as a standard for selection. This further shows that China's construction industry is gradually becoming more scientific.

In the past, earth kilns did not produce hollow bricks or fire bricks. In recent years, the height of buildings has increased daily, making it urgently necessary to reduce the weight of bricks. The use of hollow bricks has therefore increased daily. With the increasing number of factories, various boilers and chimneys all require high-temperature fire bricks, and the number of manufacturers of fire bricks has gradually increased, meeting the required industrial temperature. The greatest contribution in the brick and tile industry in recent years is the creation of facing bricks. The manufacture of facing bricks requires a high-temperature brick kiln to fire solid brick materials, as well as an aesthetically pleasing brick surface. Currently, domestic facing bricks can meet these conditions, and due to the contribution of this new domestic material, it has added much color to the field of architecture.

(2) Cement: China has had cement for a long time. In imitating Western goods among building materials, cement should be considered the first. Subsequently, cement plants were established in Shanghai and Longtan. At that time, many Chinese people were skeptical about the quality of newly produced cement, but ultimately, through testing and usage results, it was found to be no less than the best European and American cement. Once its reputation was established, sales increased daily. Cement transportation costs were very high, and foreign goods coming to China were not very numerous. At this point, it almost drove foreign imports out of the domestic market. However, Japanese products never completely disappeared. Recently, due to Japan's dumping policy, cement prices were low, and sales increased sharply. Quick-drying cement has been widely produced abroad, but China only started producing it in recent years. Cement occupies a very important position in construction, military affairs, transportation, and industry, and it is also one of the heavy industries. If the current performance can be maintained for a long time in manufacturing, and if others do not resort to excessive dumping policies, then the future of cement sales is limitless. Products made from cement, such as cement tiles, cement roofing tiles, and cinder blocks, have been increasing daily and monthly, which has also greatly benefited construction.

(3) Mosaics, Ceramic Tiles, and Glazed Tiles: Mosaics, ceramic tiles, and glazed tiles were previously not produced domestically. However, the demand for floors and wall coverings in bathrooms and other areas in new buildings is high. Therefore, the sales volume is not small. In recent years, the number of factories manufacturing them has gradually increased. Although there have been technical difficulties in terms of colors and sizes, they can be overcome. Currently, domestic products can compete with imported products. Even some merchants, to cater to social psychology, sell domestic goods as imported goods. In the future, as architecture becomes more prosperous, the uses of mosaics, ceramic tiles, and glazed tiles will increase. If more research can be done on material selection and color matching to make the products more beautiful, then the disappearance of imported products from the market is just around the corner.

(4) Paint: China originally produces lacquer and tung oil, and there are annual exports. Therefore, there should be no need to rely on others for paint. However, in recent years, buildings have become increasingly sophisticated, and the colors and gloss of paint required are beyond what domestic paint can provide. Even if it can be provided, its value is more expensive than imported paint. Therefore, foreign paints have entered the Chinese market because they are convenient to use and have a wide variety. As a result, there is no building where traces of foreign paint cannot be found. Fortunately, in recent years, some Chinese have recognized this and have established more and more paint factories. Although some of the raw materials cannot completely eliminate foreign imports, they are still manufactured by the Chinese. The quality of the materials is also improving daily, no less inferior to imported products. The variety has also increased, and all kinds of paints used for steel structures, bridges, ship hulls, doors, windows, floors, etc., can be manufactured to meet the needs of the market.

Outline of the Shanghai Municipal Hospital Hygiene Laboratory Groundbreaking Ceremony on New Year's Day

— Dong Dayou

The layout of each floor can be generally described as follows: The basement is located below the ground floor in the central part and is where boilers, electric meters, and machinery are installed. The first floor (ground floor) has a lobby in the center. The east wing contains offices, an X-ray department, and a special consulting department. The west wing contains the outpatient department. The information desk is located in the center of the lobby, surrounded by reception rooms and elevator shafts (two in total). Rooms for selling medicine, examinations, and first aid are also nearby. The second floor contains the surgical hospital and the operating department. The surgical hospital is divided into male and female sections. The male ward is in the east wing, with A-grade special, B-grade special, and general wards. The female ward and operating department are in the west wing. Each general ward can accommodate five to ten beds. There are two operating rooms, both facing north, with walls tiled with green-gray ceramic tiles and floors paved with polished stone of the same color. All of this has been carefully considered and decided after consulting with doctors. To the north of the central passageway, near the elevators, are classrooms and small testing rooms. To the south is a patient lounge with a large balcony. Various auxiliary rooms include a small kitchen, clothing storage room, nurses' station, bathrooms, and toilets. The above two points also apply to the third and fourth floors. The third floor has the pediatrics hospital in the east wing and the obstetrics department in the west wing. The pediatrics hospital has intensive care wards and general wards with glass partitions. The delivery rooms and waiting rooms of the obstetrics department are decorated similarly to the operating rooms on the first floor, and there are also nursery rooms and premature infant rooms. The layout of the fourth floor is similar to that of the first floor, but it is a male and female internal medicine hospital, so special wards replace the operating rooms on the first floor. The fifth floor only occupies the central part of the entire building and contains the kitchen, dining hall, food preparation room, and cold storage room. There is an elevator that goes directly to the basement to transport coal and other materials, and there are two food elevators to transport meals to the small kitchens on each floor.

Although the design of this building strives for economy, its contents are sufficient for current uses. It can accommodate a total of 150 beds in all departments, which can be increased to 200 if necessary.

The auxiliary buildings included in the initial project consist of a two-story building, which is one of the auxiliary buildings listed in the overall plan, located next to Fu Nan Zuo Road (referred to as "labor room" in the overall site plan). The ground floor of the building contains the funeral room, laundry room, and workshop, while the upper floor contains bedrooms.

3. Hygiene Laboratory

(Overall) Plan: The Hygiene Laboratory building faces Fu Dong Wai Road to the front and Hua Yuan Road to the west. Four auxiliary buildings are to be built on the east side, including the workers' room, animal breeding room, and vaccine manufacturing room, with the remaining land used for gardens (see the overall site plan).

(B) Initial Project: The current construction consists of the Hygiene Laboratory building and three auxiliary bungalows, namely the workers' room, animal breeding room, and vaccine manufacturing room, as well as a public toilet.

The Hygiene Laboratory building, in addition to a basement room for the boiler room, has four floors in the central part and three floors in the two wings, with a total length of approximately 41 meters and a depth of approximately 15 meters. The total floor area is approximately 1,860 square meters, and the total volume is 6,230 cubic meters. Its appearance and structure are generally the same as those of the Municipal Hospital building. The layout of each floor is as follows (see the floor plans):

The first floor (ground floor) has a lobby in the center, with passageways leading to both wings and staircases leading to the upper floors. The lobby is surrounded by an information room, waiting room, changing room, and refrigerator room. The left wing contains the material collection room, steam and dry sterilization room, washing room, and culture medium manufacturing room. The right wing contains the reception room, library, office, and director's office.

The second floor has male and female toilets on both sides of the central staircase, with a packaging room opposite them. The left wing contains the refrigerator sedimentation room, bacteria testing rooms (two in total), dissection room, and serum room. The right wing contains the vaccine manufacturing room, vaccine dilution room, vaccine testing room, vaccine grinding and dispensing room, and rabies vaccine room. The third floor has the medicine room, darkroom, and servants' room in the center. The left wing contains two exhibition rooms and two pathology rooms, as well as a large lecture hall. The right wing contains the balance room, water testing room, medicine room, nitrogen analysis room, and chemical rooms (two in total).

The fourth floor is located in the central part, rising above the two wings, with three storage rooms of various sizes.

The building is equipped with gas, compressed air, vacuum machines, both AC and DC electricity, high-voltage current, high-pressure steam, and electric refrigerators for application.

4. Remaining Remarks

The Municipal Hospital and Hygiene Laboratory projects were designed by the Architectural Office of the Municipal Central District Construction Committee in conjunction with the Bureau of Health. The budget for the first phase of the project is 400,000 yuan. The construction project was tendered by the Bureau of Public Works in November 1934. After review, Lu Genji Construction Company won the bid with a total bid price of 278,100 yuan and started construction in December, with the groundbreaking ceremony held on New Year's Day 1935. (End)

Starting New Year's Day, Fir Wood Must Be Used for Issuing Building Permits for Public and Private Buildings

In response to the request of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Municipal Bureau of Public Works formally announced yesterday.

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Works, in order to ensure that domestic fir wood is used for public and private building timber before business licenses can be issued, and to implement this starting from January 1st, specially posted a public notice yesterday to inform the public. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce requested that regulations be made to ensure that domestic fir wood must be used in all public and private buildings before business licenses can be issued. The Timber Bureau previously received instructions from the Municipal Government to review the matter and, after considering the building conditions in the city, proposed two standards for the minimum amount of domestic fir wood to be used: (1) The columns of single-story buildings must all be made of domestic fir wood; (2) The roof purlins of single-story or multi-story buildings with spans not exceeding 3.5 meters must all be made of domestic fir wood, but the diameter of the small end must not be less than 12 centimeters. These standards have been submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and will be implemented starting from January 1st, 1935. This notice is hereby issued for general knowledge.

News from the Architectural World in the Past Year (Selected Notes)

— Huai Xiang

The Da Xin Department Store, designed by the Jintai Engineering Company, has been awarded to the Fu Construction Company. The land for the Father Lo Shenfu Road tennis court was donated by the American oil tycoon, and the Zhongshan Hospital, also designed by Jintai, is being built on it. The drawings have been revised repeatedly, and the Wang Yanji Construction Company is undertaking the construction, which has now begun.

The address of the Hongying Library has been temporarily set as part of the Zhongshan Hospital, designed by Lian Jian Architect and built by Tang Xiuji.

The 22-story building of the Si Hang Reserve Committee, designed by Dak, and the Bailao Hui Road Building, designed by Ye Guang, were completed in the same year.

The foundation stone laying ceremony for the Shibu Seafood Market, designed by Xingye Architect, was held on New Year's Day. Chen Gongbo, Minister of Industry, came from Beijing to participate.

The Municipal Sports Hall, Museum, and Library in the central district, presided over by architect Dong Dayou, have begun construction. The groundbreaking ceremony for the Municipal Hospital was held on New Year's Day.

Architect Fan Wenzhao and architect Li Huibo had negotiations over the design of the Guangdong Provincial Government building, which were later peacefully resolved.

Liu Hongsheng's plan to invite a Western architect to design the new China Merchants Bureau building aroused opposition from the Chinese Institute of Architects, which strongly argued with Liu.

The plan for the new Bank of China building has been finalized and will be jointly planned by architect Lu Quan Shou and the Gong He Yang Xing firm.

Construction engineer Gu Pengcheng founded the Zhongdu Engineering Company in the Hengli Building.

Architect Gu Daosheng joined Jiu Ji Construction Company, architect Xi Fuquan left Qiming and joined the Gong Li Business Company, presiding over design affairs, forming a situation of flying elephants and falling scholars.

The Hangzhou Jianye Bank, designed by architect Li Jinpei, will be completed soon. The New Capital Theater in Nanjing is under construction and is being built by Fei Xinji.

British architects Keith and Tuosuiwei came from Singapore and set up an architectural firm in Hamilton Building, appointing Yang Xianbang as the Chinese manager.

The 18-story building of the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank, designed by Xin Ruihe and built by Tao Guiji, has started construction. The Yong'an Bank Building, designed by Hashad, has also been awarded to Tao Guiji and construction has begun.

The Jiangzhe Bank is building its own building, designed by Tonghe Yanghang and built by Zhang Jiguang's Xie Shun. The project is underway.

The Hangzhou Central Bank and Changshu Transportation Bank, designed by architect Miao Kaibo, have been completed. The Nanchang Central Bank, which is being designed, will also begin construction soon.

Architect Lin Ruiji moved his office to the Zhonghui Building. Architect Li Yang'an left Li Jinpei's office and set up an office with architect Lin Xu.

The plans for the new buildings of the Hubei Provincial Government have been temporarily suspended due to the earthquake, and the drawings prepared by Yang Xiliu have also been cancelled.

The Continental Department Store was designed by architect Zhuang Jun to add another floor.

The Qingdao Continental Bank, designed by architect Luo Bangjie, has been completed. The Jinan Continental Bank project is underway.

The entire building of Shanghai Middle School, designed by architect Qi Minghe, has been completed and moved into use.

The architecture department jointly run by the Architectural Society and the Business School of Hujiang University has opened, with architect Huang Jiahua in charge of all educational affairs.

Yan Ming, Ya Jie, Yun, Qin, Xi Hao, Li Touming, Ying Dai, Mei Zhenshi, A Shou, Yang Dehui, Zhenmu, Shu Jie, gentlemen and ladies, thank you very much for the contributions you made in December! The payment for the contributions has been settled. Please go to the accounting department of this hall between 2:00 PM and 4:00 PM from the 8th to the 10th and from the 16th to the 20th of this month (excluding Sundays) with your seal to receive the payment. Sincerely, Shen Bao Architectural Special Issue Department
